#### 50. [P2] xmltv_parser.dart:~143 — Strict utf8.decoder aborts the entire EPG parse on the first non-UTF-8 byte (ISO-8859-1 / windows-1251 Europea · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** XmltvParser.parse — grep the pipeline `.transform(utf8.decoder)` on `byteStream` just above `.transform(XmlEventDecoder())`.
- **Current code:**
```dart
    final eventStream = byteStream
        .transform(utf8.decoder)
        .transform(XmlEventDecoder())
        .expand((list) => list);
```
- **Fix:** Replace `utf8.decoder` with a lenient decoder so a stray non-UTF-8 byte produces a replacement char (U+FFFD) instead of throwing and killing the whole feed:
    final eventStream = byteStream
        .transform(const Utf8Decoder(allowMalformed: true))
        .transform(XmlEventDecoder())
        .expand((list) => list);
DECISION: use `const Utf8Decoder(allowMalformed: true)` rather than sniffing the XML declaration's encoding attribute — the latter is a larger change (need to buffer the prolog, map charset names to Dart codecs, and Dart lacks built-in ISO-8859-x/windows-1251 codecs without a package). allowMalformed keeps the feed usable (a handful of mangled accented chars) instead of a total refresh failure. No new import — Utf8Decoder is already available via `dart:convert` (line 2).
- **Blast radius:** Self-contained. A feed that is genuinely UTF-8 is unaffected (allowMalformed only changes behavior on invalid sequences). Downstream XmlEventDecoder receives valid Dart strings either way. Titles/descriptions on truly non-UTF-8 feeds will contain U+FFFD in place of accented bytes — acceptable degradation vs total loss. Interacts with the _maybeUngzip cancel fix (line 226/231): previously a decode throw leaked the download; with allowMalformed there is no throw, so that leak path for this cause disappears too.
- **Acceptance:** Unit test test/xmltv_malformed_utf8_test.dart: feed parse() a byteStream containing `<tv><channel id="c"><display-name>Caf\xE9</display-name></channel><programme start="20260101000000 +0000" stop="20260101010000 +0000" channel="c"><title>A</title></programme></tv>` where \xE9 is the raw Latin-1 é byte; assert parse() completes without throwing and the returned channelMap contains key 'c' (title 'A' inserted). Before the fix this throws FormatException.
- **Notes:** Premise (European feeds serve non-UTF-8) is plausible but provider-dependent; implementer should confirm at least one real feed exhibits it, though the fix is safe to apply unconditionally.

#### 51. [P1] xmltv_parser.dart:~191 — Window filter keys on start_utc — with Past-days=0 every currently-airing programme is dropped, so isStale() s

- **Anchor:** XmltvParser.parse — inside `case 'programme':` of the XmlEndElementEvent branch; grep `if (p.startUtc >= windowStartEpoch &&` followed by `p.startUtc <= windowEndEpoch)`.
- **Current code:**
```dart
              if (p.startUtc >= windowStartEpoch &&
                  p.startUtc <= windowEndEpoch) {
```
- **Fix:** Change the insert filter to interval-overlap semantics matching deleteStalePrograms (which keeps rows with stop_utc >= windowStart). A programme is inside the window when it has not yet ended AND has already started (or starts) within the window. Replace the snippet with:
              if (p.stopUtc > windowStartEpoch &&
                  p.startUtc <= windowEndEpoch) {
Rationale: deleteStalePrograms (sql.dart:2812) deletes where `stop_utc < windowStart`, i.e. KEEPS where `stop_utc >= windowStart`; the insert filter must agree so a programme airing right now (started before now=windowStart at pastDays=0, ends after now) is inserted and survives GC. With pastDays=0, windowStart=now, so `p.stopUtc > now` keeps the currently-airing programme, and isStale() (epg_service.dart:83-87, needs start_utc<=now AND stop_utc>now) can find it. DECISION: use `stopUtc > windowStartEpoch` (strict >) to mirror deleteStalePrograms' `stop_utc < windowStart` boundary exactly (rows with stop_utc == windowStart are deleted, so also skip them on insert to avoid churn).
- **Blast radius:** Self-contained to xmltv_parser.dart. Slightly increases inserted rows (programmes that started before the window but end inside it — at most one in-progress programme per channel at windowStart). No schema change. The `skipped` counter (line 196) drops correspondingly. Verify no unit test asserts the old start-based filter count. Interacts with the truncated-timestamp finding (line 290): a programme whose stop parses to 0 now fails `p.stopUtc > windowStartEpoch` and is skipped — same net effect as before, so fixing 290 is still independently needed.
- **Acceptance:** Unit test test/xmltv_window_overlap_test.dart: with windowStartEpoch = 1000 (== now) and windowEndEpoch = 1000+3*86400, feed a programme start=500 stop=2000 (airing now, started before window) via parse(); assert onBatch received it (previously skipped because start 500 < windowStart 1000). Second assertion: a fully-past programme start=100 stop=200 is still skipped.
- **Notes:** verdict CONFIRMED. This is the root cause of the isStale-always-true → hourly re-download loop at pastDays=0 (the storage-saving setting the help text recommends).

#### 52. [P3] xmltv_parser.dart:~290 — _parseXmltvTime zeroes truncated timestamps (<14 digits) and mis-parses colon-form offsets — whole feeds silen

- **Anchor:** XmltvParser._parseXmltvTime — grep `if (dt.length < 14) return 0;` and the subsequent `dt.substring(0, 4)` year parse.
- **Current code:**
```dart
    if (dt.length < 14) return 0;

    final year = int.tryParse(dt.substring(0, 4)) ?? 0;
    final month = int.tryParse(dt.substring(4, 6)) ?? 1;
    final day = int.tryParse(dt.substring(6, 8)) ?? 1;
    final hour = int.tryParse(dt.substring(8, 10)) ?? 0;
    final min = int.tryParse(dt.substring(10, 12)) ?? 0;
    final sec = int.tryParse(dt.substring(12, 14)) ?? 0;
```
- **Fix:** Pad right-truncated XMLTV date-times to 14 digits per the spec (missing lower-order fields default to their minimum: month/day→01 via the padding making them '01'? — NO: bare padding with '0' would make a truncated 'YYYY' become 'YYYY0000000000' → month 00, day 00, invalid). Instead pad the DATE-TIME string to 14 chars using a template of minimum-valid values so missing month/day become 01 and missing time fields become 00. Replace the `if (dt.length < 14) return 0;` guard with a pad step and drop the hard-zero. Concretely, replace the snippet's first line and keep the parses but source them from a padded string:
    // XMLTV allows right-truncation; pad missing lower-order fields to their
    // minimum (month/day=01, time=00) per the DTD.
    const tmpl = '00000101000000'; // YYYY MM DD HH mm ss minimums
    var d = dt;
    if (d.length < 14) {
      if (d.length < 4) return 0; // no usable year → unparseable
      d = d + tmpl.substring(d.length);
    } else if (d.length > 14) {
      d = d.substring(0, 14);
    }
    final year = int.tryParse(d.substring(0, 4)) ?? 0;
    final month = int.tryParse(d.substring(4, 6)) ?? 1;
    final day = int.tryParse(d.substring(6, 8)) ?? 1;
    final hour = int.tryParse(d.substring(8, 10)) ?? 0;
    final min = int.tryParse(d.substring(10, 12)) ?? 0;
    final sec = int.tryParse(d.substring(12, 14)) ?? 0;
DECISION: template pad (not zero-pad) so a 'YYYYMM' truncation yields day=01 not day=00 (DateTime.utc(y,m,0) would roll to the previous month). Guard length<4 as the only true-unparseable case. The colon-offset half of this finding is fixed in the line-305 spec entry — do not duplicate the tz edit here. Also add a one-time diagnostic: in parse(), after the loop, if `inserted == 0 && skipped > 0` log `AppLog.warn('XMLTV: 0 in-window programmes from $skipped total — possible timestamp/window mismatch for host=...')` so a wholesale-discarded feed is visible.
- **Blast radius:** Self-contained to _parseXmltvTime plus one optional warn in parse(). Padding changes previously-zeroed timestamps into real epoch values, so those programmes now pass the window filter and get inserted (intended). Verify no test asserts _parseXmltvTime returns 0 for a 12-digit input. The added parse()-level warn touches the counters already in scope (inserted/skipped).
- **Acceptance:** Unit test test/xmltv_time_truncated_test.dart: assert XmltvParser via @visibleForTesting-exposed _parseXmltvTime (or an extracted top-level fn) that _parseXmltvTime('20260703') == DateTime.utc(2026,7,3).millisecondsSinceEpoch~/1000 and _parseXmltvTime('202607031230') == DateTime.utc(2026,7,3,12,30).millisecondsSinceEpoch~/1000, and _parseXmltvTime('202') == 0.
- **Notes:** Requires making _parseXmltvTime testable (currently private static) — recommend adding `@visibleForTesting` re-export or extracting to a top-level function; note import 'package:flutter/foundation.dart' for @visibleForTesting if used in a non-flutter file, else keep test in the same library via part/export.

#### 53. [P3] xmltv_parser.dart:~305 — Timezone offsets with a colon (+05:30) lose their minutes; missing offset defaults to UTC instead of local

- **Anchor:** XmltvParser._parseXmltvTime — grep `if (tz.length >= 5) {` and the `tz.substring(1, 3)` / `tz.substring(3, 5)` slices; also the `'+0000'` default at the `final tz = spaceIdx > 0 ...` line.
- **Current code:**
```dart
    if (tz.length >= 5) {
      final sign = tz[0] == '-' ? 1 : -1; // subtract east offset to get UTC
      final tzH = int.tryParse(tz.substring(1, 3)) ?? 0;
      final tzM = int.tryParse(tz.substring(3, 5)) ?? 0;
      epochSecs += sign * (tzH * 3600 + tzM * 60);
    }
```
- **Fix:** Normalize the offset token by stripping a colon before slicing, so '+05:30' → '+0530'. Replace the snippet with:
    final tzNorm = tz.replaceAll(':', '');
    if (tzNorm.length >= 5 && (tzNorm[0] == '+' || tzNorm[0] == '-')) {
      final sign = tzNorm[0] == '-' ? 1 : -1; // subtract east offset to get UTC
      final tzH = int.tryParse(tzNorm.substring(1, 3));
      final tzM = int.tryParse(tzNorm.substring(3, 5));
      if (tzH != null && tzM != null) {
        epochSecs += sign * (tzH * 3600 + tzM * 60);
      } else {
        AppLog.warn('XMLTV: unparseable tz offset "$tz" — treated as UTC');
      }
    }
DECISION on the missing-offset half: the XMLTV DTD technically treats an offset-less timestamp as local time, but the app has no reliable device-vs-provider timezone to apply and the current '+0000' default is the pragmatic behavior that most real feeds (which almost always include an offset) rely on. KEEP the '+0000' default at the `final tz = spaceIdx > 0 ? ... : '+0000';` line — do NOT change it — to avoid shifting the majority of correctly-offset feeds. Only fix the colon-parsing and add the diagnostic. This is a deliberate scope limit; note it in the commit.
- **Blast radius:** Self-contained to _parseXmltvTime. Fixes IST/half-hour-offset feeds (+05:30, +04:30, +09:30, etc.) that were silently 30 min off. The added guard (`tzNorm[0] == '+' || '-'`) prevents mis-slicing a malformed token. Shares the _parseXmltvTime method with the line-290 fix — apply both in one editing pass; the tz block is BELOW the date-parse block so editing 305 first then 290 (higher up) keeps offsets stable, or edit the whole method body at once.
- **Acceptance:** Unit test in test/xmltv_time_truncated_test.dart (same file as line-290): assert _parseXmltvTime('20260703120000 +05:30') == DateTime.utc(2026,7,3,6,30).millisecondsSinceEpoch~/1000 (12:30 IST → 07:00 UTC... verify arithmetic: 12:00 +05:30 → 06:30 UTC), and _parseXmltvTime('20260703120000 -0400') == DateTime.utc(2026,7,3,16,0)...~/1000. Confirm '+0530' (no colon) still parses identically.
- **Notes:** Do NOT change the '+0000' missing-offset default — decision recorded above. The colon-strip is the only behavior change here.

```dart
    var db = SqliteDatabase(path: "${await Utils.appDir}/db.sqlite");
    var migrations = SqliteMigrations()
      ..add(SqliteMigration(1, (tx) async {
```
- **Fix:** Make the real migration chains testable and assert two invariants. #### 55. [P1] db_factory.dart:~53 — ON DELETE CASCADE declared on channel_http_headers / movie_positions but PRAGMA foreign_keys never enabled — o

- **Anchor:** DbFactory._createDB, migration 1 CREATE TABLE blocks — grep `"channel_http_headers"` and `"movie_positions"`; the CASCADE lines are `FOREIGN KEY (channel_id) REFERENCES channels(id) ON DELETE CASCADE`.             "ignore_ssl" integer DEFAULT 0,
```dart
            FOREIGN KEY (channel_id) REFERENCES channels(id) ON DELETE CASCADE
        );
```

AND media_type NOT IN (<placeholders>))` with the same bind list, and the same for channel_http_headers. Leave the CASCADE declarations in db_factory.dart as-is (harmless documentation). #### 56. [P2] db_factory.dart:~949 — Fresh installs are never pre-marked fix537-done; a new user builds old-shape/dead browse indexes at first refr · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** DbFactory._createDB, migration 39 — grep `SqliteMigration(39` / `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS app_meta`. Coupled to sql.dart `runPendingIndexMaintenance` `const marker = 'fix537_index_rebuild_done'`.
- **Current code:**
```dart
        await tx.execute(
          'CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS app_meta'
          ' (key TEXT PRIMARY KEY, value TEXT);',
        );
      }))
```
- **Fix:** In migration 39, after creating app_meta, pre-mark the fix537 maintenance done WHEN THE DB IS FRESH (channels empty) so a brand-new install skips the one-time deferred pass entirely. Replace the migration-39 body with:
```
await tx.execute(
  'CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS app_meta'
  ' (key TEXT PRIMARY KEY, value TEXT);',
);
// fix537 maintenance only reshapes indexes that migration 1/29/30/33 created
// with the OLD (cat_enabled) shape over EXISTING rows. On a fresh install the
// channels table is empty, so there is nothing to reshape — pre-mark the
// marker so runPendingIndexMaintenance() no-ops on first real launch.
final chRow = await tx.getOptional('SELECT 1 FROM channels LIMIT 1;');
if (chRow == null) {
  await tx.execute(
    "INSERT OR REPLACE INTO app_meta (key, value) VALUES ('fix537_index_rebuild_done', '1');",
  );
}
```
Decision: chose the marker-only pre-seed (smallest change) over rewriting the tail migrations to emit final index shapes. This is safe because on a fresh install the FIRST refresh's `Sql.withDroppedBrowseIndexes` recreate loop reads sqlite_master and will still recreate whatever indexes exist at that time; pre-marking only prevents the redundant next-launch drop/rebuild/VACUUM. Use the literal marker string `fix537_index_rebuild_done` (must match sql.dart:1525 exactly). Note `tx.getOptional` is the sqlite_async API used elsewhere; if unavailable in the migration tx use `tx.getAll(...).isEmpty`.
- **Blast radius:** Runs inside the migration-39 transaction on every install; the `IF channels empty` guard makes it a no-op for upgraders (their marker is set/legacy-detected by runPendingIndexMaintenance as today). Does NOT stop migrations 29/30/33/37 from creating cat_enabled-shaped and *_safe indexes on a fresh empty table (cheap — empty). The dead-index list (idx_browse_cat, idx_browse_cat_safe, index_channel_name, idx_channel_adult, idx_channel_divider) will still be CREATED then never dropped on a fresh install that skips maintenance — if that matters, the alternative (rewrite tail migrations to not create dead shapes) is the larger fix; recommend the marker-only change and file the dead-index-on-fresh cleanup separately. Second-file awareness: behavior is defined jointly with sql.dart runPendingIndexMaintenance (L1600-1618) which already honors the marker.
- **Acceptance:** TEST: `test/fresh_install_marker_test.dart` name 'fresh migration marks fix537 done'. Run the full DbFactory migration chain (via the buildMigrations() extracted in finding 1) against a fresh empty DB, then assert `SELECT value FROM app_meta WHERE key='fix537_index_rebuild_done'` returns '1'. Second test 'upgrade with existing channels does not pre-mark': create v38 schema, insert one channels row, migrate to head, assert the marker is NULL (so real maintenance still runs once). DEVICE follow-up (optional): on the onn 4K box, a truly fresh install + first refresh should NOT log 'fix542: deferred index maintenance starting…' on the second launch.
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED: migration 39 (db_factory.dart:962-965) creates only app_meta and writes no marker; main.dart:104 gates runPendingIndexMaintenance behind hasSources so it cannot run on launch 1; the marker string is defined at sql.dart:1525. Verify the exact set of indexes a fresh chain leaves behind before deciding whether the dead-index cleanup also needs the larger tail-migration rewrite.

#### 57. [P1] db_factory.dart:~1240 — EpgDbFactory memoizes a FAILED open future permanently — one transient open/migration error kills all EPG feat

- **Anchor:** EpgDbFactory — `static Future<SqliteDatabase>? _dbFuture;` and getter `static Future<SqliteDatabase> get db async { return _dbFuture ??= _createDB(); }` (grep `_dbFuture ??=`).
- **Current code:**
```dart
  static Future<SqliteDatabase>? _dbFuture;

  static Future<SqliteDatabase> get db async {
    return _dbFuture ??= _createDB();
  }
```
- **Fix:** Keep the concurrent-caller dedup (fix644) but clear the memo on failure so the next caller retries. Replace the getter body with:
```
static Future<SqliteDatabase> get db async {
  final existing = _dbFuture;
  if (existing != null) return existing;
  final future = _createDB();
  _dbFuture = future;
  try {
    return await future;
  } catch (e) {
    // fix: a transient open/migration failure (e.g. SQLITE_BUSY under
    // cross-isolate contention) must not permanently poison the memo.
    // Only clear if it is still OUR future (a concurrent successful retry
    // may have replaced it).
    if (identical(_dbFuture, future)) _dbFuture = null;
    rethrow;
  }
}
```
Decision: use `identical()` guard before nulling so a concurrent caller's in-flight/succeeded future is not clobbered. This preserves fix644's dedup (concurrent callers within a successful open still share `future`).
- **Blast radius:** Only the EpgDbFactory.db getter. Callers: guide grid, now/next, EPG search, EPG refresh — all currently latch on first failure; after the fix they retry on next access (correct). No schema change. Note the SAME pattern must be applied to DbFactory.db (see the P3 DbFactory finding) — implement one shared idiom.
- **Acceptance:** TEST: `test/epg_db_retry_test.dart` name 'failed open clears memo and allows retry'. Inject a _createDB that throws on first call and succeeds on second (extract the factory into a swappable field or use @visibleForTesting seam), assert first `await EpgDbFactory.db` throws, then second `await EpgDbFactory.db` returns a DB. If no seam exists, this is STATIC: confirm the getter nulls `_dbFuture` on catch before rethrow (assert via code inspection). DEVICE: cannot deterministically reproduce SQLITE_BUSY cross-isolate contention without the workmanager isolate holding the writer lock.
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED verbatim at db_factory.dart:1237-1241: `_dbFuture ??= _createDB()` with no catch/reset. _createDB awaits migrations.migrate(db) at L1179 which runs a writeTransaction that can throw SqliteException code 5.

#### 58. [P3] db_factory.dart:~715 — Multi-version upgrade runs the heavy migration tail (mig35 FTS retokenize + mig37 four ~1.17M-row index builds · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** DbFactory._createDB migrations — mig35 `SqliteMigration(35` (FTS repopulate: `INSERT INTO channels_fts(rowid, name) SELECT id, name FROM channels`), mig37 `SqliteMigration(37` (four `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_*_safe`), mig38 `SqliteMigration(38` (`ANALYZE;`). The blocking await is `await migrations.migrate(db);` (grep `await migrations.migrate(db)`).
- **Current code:**
```dart
        await tx.execute('''
          INSERT INTO channels_fts(rowid, name)
          SELECT id, name FROM channels;
        ''');
```
- **Fix:** Defer the DATA-heavy work behind app_meta markers run post-first-frame (the established fix542 pattern in Sql.runPendingIndexMaintenance / main.dart:114), leaving the migrations to create EMPTY structures only. Concrete, minimal-risk decision: (1) In migration 35, keep the DROP/CREATE of the channels_fts virtual table and triggers but REMOVE the `INSERT INTO channels_fts(rowid, name) SELECT id, name FROM channels;` backfill; instead let the existing fix593-style self-heal repopulate it — but channels_fts has NO device-side self-heal today (only programmes_fts does), so you must add one: extend `Sql.runPendingIndexMaintenance` (or a sibling deferred routine gated by a new marker e.g. `channels_fts_backfill_done`) to run `INSERT INTO channels_fts(channels_fts) VALUES('rebuild');` once when channels is non-empty and fts is empty. (2) Migrations 37 and 38 are ALREADY effectively duplicated by the deferred fix542 maintenance (which rebuilds the browse indexes and runs PRAGMA optimize); the cleanest change is to make migrations 37/38 no-ops on an upgrade-over-populated-catalog by guarding: only build the *_safe indexes / ANALYZE when channels is empty (fresh), else rely on runPendingIndexMaintenance. Because this is a P3 with real regression risk (Safe-Mode browse depends on the *_safe indexes + ANALYZE existing), RECOMMENDED path: do NOT rewrite the migrations; instead ONLY move mig35's FTS backfill and mig38's ANALYZE out (the two largest full-scans), keep mig37 index builds where they are (they are already memory-pragma-wrapped), and add the channels_fts deferred backfill described in (1). State the decision in the migration comment.
- **Blast radius:** Touches db_factory.dart migrations 35/38 AND lib/backend/sql.dart (new deferred channels_fts backfill + marker) AND depends on main.dart already calling the deferred routine after first frame. High regression risk: channel search returns empty until the deferred FTS backfill completes; Safe-Mode browse depends on ANALYZE stats — deferring ANALYZE means the planner is briefly blind on first post-upgrade launch. Must confirm main.dart's post-first-frame hook runs the new backfill and that the window is acceptable.
- **Acceptance:** DEVICE: on the onn 4K box (or a Shield, closer to the 272k+/1M-row case), sideload the current APK over a pre-mig35 install with a >=1M-row catalog and confirm the app draws its first frame without ANR (observe: no black screen / no 'not responding'), then confirm channel search returns results within N seconds after launch once the deferred backfill logs complete. This CANNOT be proven without a device + a large real DB; a synthetic 1M-row DB in a test can measure migrate() wall-time but not Android ANR behavior. TEST (partial): assert migration 35 no longer contains the backfill INSERT and that the deferred backfill routine repopulates channels_fts from a populated channels table.
- **Notes:** Confirmed the heavy statements exist: mig35 backfill (db_factory.dart:732-735), mig37 four *_safe CREATE INDEX (795-860), mig38 `ANALYZE;` (928), all after `await migrations.migrate(db)` at L1037 which the app awaits before runApp. NOTE the migration tx is already wrapped in temp_store=FILE + cache_size=-32768 (L1033-1036) — the OOM angle is mitigated; the risk is wall-time/ANR, not memory. Verify the ANR premise on-device before reshaping working migrations.

#### 59. [P3] db_factory.dart:~1037 — No down-migrations on either DB: installing an older APK throws MigrationError on every open — app unusable af

- **Anchor:** DbFactory._createDB `await migrations.migrate(db);` and EpgDbFactory._createDB `await migrations.migrate(db);` — every `SqliteMigration(N, fn)` is constructed with NO downMigration argument (grep `SqliteMigration(` — none pass a down closure).
- **Current code:**
```dart
    await migrations.migrate(db);
    try {
      await db.execute('PRAGMA cache_size = -2000;');
    } catch (_) {}
```
- **Fix:** Chosen scope (smallest correct, matches the finding's 'at minimum'): catch MigrationError at open in BOTH _createDB bodies, log a clear downgrade diagnostic, and rethrow (do NOT silently wipe user data). Wrap the migrate call:
```
try {
  await migrations.migrate(db);
} on MigrationError catch (e) {
  AppLog.error('DB open failed: app was likely downgraded to an older '
      'version than this database was created for (db.sqlite). '
      'Reinstall the newer version or clear app data to reset. Detail: $e');
  rethrow;
}
```
Apply the analogous block in EpgDbFactory._createDB (message names epg.sqlite). `MigrationError` is exported by `package:sqlite_async` (already imported). Decision: do NOT auto-register no-op down-migrations — a down-migration that no-ops an ADD COLUMN/CREATE INDEX would let an OLDER code version open a NEWER-shaped DB whose new columns it doesn't know about, risking silent wrong behavior; failing loudly with a clear message is safer for a sideloaded app. If the owner later wants graceful downgrade, that is a separate, deliberate change.
- **Blast radius:** Both _createDB bodies (db.sqlite and epg.sqlite). No behavior change on the normal upgrade/fresh path (migrate only throws MigrationError when stored version > code version). Improves the log/diagnostic on downgrade; the app still cannot open (by design) until reinstall/clear-data. Pairs with the EpgDbFactory failed-future reset (P1 finding) so the downgrade error is retried-and-re-thrown cleanly rather than latched.
- **Acceptance:** TEST: `test/downgrade_migration_test.dart` name 'opening a newer DB with older chain throws MigrationError'. Migrate a temp DB to head with the full builder, then attempt `migrate` with a builder truncated to an EARLIER max version and assert it throws `MigrationError`. STATIC: confirm both _createDB bodies wrap migrate() in `on MigrationError` and rethrow (not swallow). DEVICE (optional): sideload an older APK over a newer install and confirm the log shows the downgrade message rather than a bare crash.
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED: no SqliteMigration in either chain passes a down closure; sqlite_async's migrate() throws MigrationError when currentVersion > target. db.sqlite head is v43, epg.sqlite head is v2.

#### 60. [P3] db_factory.dart:~1092 — DbFactory.db retains the exact concurrent-open race fix644 fixed for the EPG DB (`_db ??= await _createDB()`)

- **Anchor:** DbFactory — `static SqliteDatabase? _db;`, `static TimedWriteContext? _timedDb;` and getter `static Future<SqliteWriteContext> get db async { _db ??= await _createDB(); ... }` (grep `_db ??= await _createDB`).
- **Current code:**
```dart
  static Future<SqliteWriteContext> get db async {
    _db ??= await _createDB();
    // fix238: hand callers a timing wrapper (slow-query logging) instead of the
    // raw database. The wrapper exposes the SqliteWriteContext surface all
    // callers use; the raw instance is retained in _db for lifecycle.
    _timedDb ??= TimedWriteContext(_db!);
    return _timedDb!;
  }
```
- **Fix:** Memoize the OPEN FUTURE, not the awaited result — same idiom as the EPG fix (P1 finding), including failure-reset. Add a field `static Future<SqliteDatabase>? _dbFuture;` next to `_db`, and rewrite the getter:
```
static Future<SqliteWriteContext> get db async {
  var future = _dbFuture;
  if (future == null) {
    future = _createDB();
    _dbFuture = future;
  }
  final SqliteDatabase database;
  try {
    database = await future;
  } catch (e) {
    if (identical(_dbFuture, future)) _dbFuture = null;
    rethrow;
  }
  _db ??= database;
  _timedDb ??= TimedWriteContext(_db!);
  return _timedDb!;
}
```
This keeps `_db`/`_timedDb` for lifecycle/logging while ensuring N in-flight callers share ONE _createDB() (no duplicate migration/ANALYZE, no leaked second SqliteDatabase) and a failed open is retried. Keep the fix238 comment.
- **Blast radius:** Only the DbFactory.db getter. Every DB consumer in the app (all of sql.dart) goes through this getter — the change is transparent (same TimedWriteContext returned). Removes the risk of two writers contending on db.sqlite for the session. Mirror of the EpgDbFactory fix; implement both with the identical failure-reset idiom.
- **Acceptance:** TEST: `test/db_factory_single_open_test.dart` name 'concurrent db getter awaits share one open'. With a _createDB seam that increments a counter and delays, fire `Future.wait([DbFactory.db, DbFactory.db, DbFactory.db])` and assert the counter == 1. Second test 'failed open is retried' (throw-then-succeed seam). If no seam is added, STATIC: confirm the getter memoizes `_dbFuture` before awaiting and nulls it on catch. Cannot prove the multi-minute-upgrade race window without a large DB, but the counter test proves single-open semantics deterministically.
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED at db_factory.dart:1091-1098: null check happens before the await, so concurrent callers each start _createDB(). Contrast with the fixed EPG pattern at L1237-1241 which this finding says to copy (and which itself needs the failure-reset from the P1 finding).

#### 61. [P3] db_factory.dart:~1216 — Every-open fire-and-forget programmes_fts self-heal can trigger a spurious full trigram rebuild while a backgr · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** EpgDbFactory._selfHealProgrammesFts — grep `_selfHealProgrammesFts`; the trigger is `if (progCount > 0 && ftsCount != progCount)` followed by `INSERT INTO programmes_fts(programmes_fts) VALUES('rebuild')`. Called fire-and-forget via `unawaited(_selfHealProgrammesFts(db));`.
- **Current code:**
```dart
      if (progCount > 0 && ftsCount != progCount) {
        AppLog.warn('EpgDb: programmes_fts stale (fts=$ftsCount vs '
            'programmes=$progCount) — rebuilding (fix593)');
        await db
            .execute("INSERT INTO programmes_fts(programmes_fts) VALUES('rebuild');");
```
- **Fix:** Guard the rebuild so it does not fire during (or immediately after the start of) an EPG refresh, where a count mismatch is EXPECTED (programmes get inserted per batch; programmes_fts is rebuilt only at refresh end). Decision: use the recency of epg_refresh_log rather than adding a new in-progress flag (epg_refresh_log already exists; rows carry last_refreshed_utc). Before the rebuild branch, read the most recent refresh time and skip if a refresh completed/started very recently OR — more robust against 'refresh still running' — skip when any refresh is in-flight. Since epg_refresh_log only records COMPLETED refreshes (last_refreshed_utc set at end), add an EpgService in-progress signal: have EpgService set an app_meta-style marker (or a static, but statics are per-isolate — the refresh runs in the workmanager isolate, so a DB-backed marker is REQUIRED). Concrete minimal change in _selfHealProgrammesFts: wrap the rebuild in a guard
```
final running = await db.getOptional(
  "SELECT value FROM epg_refresh_state WHERE key='refresh_in_progress'");
if (running != null && running['value'] == '1') {
  AppLog.info('EpgDb: skipping programmes_fts heal — refresh in progress');
  return;
}
```
and have EpgService write/clear `refresh_in_progress` in epg.sqlite at refresh start/end (SECOND FILE: lib/backend/epg_service.dart; create the tiny state table in EpgDbFactory migration 2 or a new migration 3). If adding cross-isolate state is deemed too large for a P3, the SMALLER accepted alternative is a debounce: only rebuild when the mismatch persists across two opens — record `last_fts_mismatch_utc` in epg_refresh_log/app_meta and require a prior mismatch older than e.g. 60s with counts still unequal before rebuilding. RECOMMENDED: the debounce alternative (single-file, no isolate coordination) unless the owner wants the explicit in-progress marker.
- **Blast radius:** If implementing the marker: SECOND FILE lib/backend/epg_service.dart (set/clear the DB marker around a refresh) AND a new EPG migration to create the marker/state table — which itself must satisfy the migration-parity test from finding 1. If implementing the debounce: contained to _selfHealProgrammesFts plus one persisted timestamp. Either way, statics won't work (workmanager runs a separate isolate — Dart statics are per-isolate), so any in-progress flag MUST be DB-backed. Risk of the guard: if a refresh crashes without clearing the marker, the heal is suppressed until the next successful refresh — mitigate with a staleness check (ignore the marker if older than the max plausible refresh duration).
- **Acceptance:** TEST: `test/programmes_fts_selfheal_guard_test.dart` name 'heal skipped when refresh in progress'. Seed programmes (count N) and an empty programmes_fts, set the in-progress marker, run _selfHealProgrammesFts (extract to a testable seam), assert programmes_fts is STILL empty and no rebuild ran; then clear the marker, run again, assert programmes_fts count == N. DEVICE: on the onn box, start a background EPG refresh and open the app mid-refresh; confirm the log does NOT show 'programmes_fts stale — rebuilding' during the refresh window (this is the observed regression scenario and can only be fully confirmed on-device with a ~1.5M-row EPG).
- **Notes:** Confirmed at db_factory.dart:1207-1229: plain count compare with an unconditional rebuild on mismatch, no refresh-state awareness, called unawaited from _createDB (L1201). epg_service performs its own rebuild at refresh end (finding cites epg_service.dart:245). Verify epg_refresh_log semantics (completed-only) and whether EpgService can cheaply publish an in-progress marker before choosing marker vs debounce.

#### 62. [P1] xtream.dart:~63 — Xtream refresh downloads and json-decodes all six catalog responses concurrently on the main isolate — multi-h · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** getXtream() — the `var results = await Future.wait([` block calling the six getXtreamHttpData(...) fetches (getLiveStreams first)
- **Current code:**
```dart
  var results = await Future.wait([
    getXtreamHttpData(getLiveStreams, source),
    getXtreamHttpData(getLiveStreamCategories, source),
    getXtreamHttpData(getVods, source),
    getXtreamHttpData(getVodCategories, source),
    getXtreamHttpData(getSeries, source),
    getXtreamHttpData(getSeriesCategories, source),
  ]);
```
- **Fix:** Two coordinated changes. (A) MEMORY: stop holding all six decoded trees at the Future.wait join. Replace the single Future.wait with THREE sequential per-content-type fetch+process passes so each type's decoded tree is released (goes out of scope, eligible for GC) before the next is fetched. Concretely: fetch live+liveCats, run processJsonList/processXtream into contentStatements, then null out the local refs (or scope them in a `{ }` block / helper) before fetching vod+vodCats, then series+seriesCats. The existing `results[0..5] != null` gate logic at lines 83-151 must be rewritten to consume the per-pass results instead of an array. (B) UI-BLOCK: move the synchronous jsonDecode off the UI isolate. In getXtreamHttpData (line 386) replace `return jsonDecode(response.body);` with an isolate-offloaded decode using the SAME pattern already used for EPG matching — grep `compute(` in lib/backend to find whether the repo uses flutter `compute` or `Isolate.run`; use `return await Isolate.run(() => jsonDecode(bodyStr));` (add `import 'dart:isolate';`) OR `await compute(jsonDecode, response.body)` if `package:flutter/foundation.dart` is already imported there. Prefer Isolate.run to avoid a Flutter dependency in this backend file. Do NOT attempt a streaming parse in this change — that is a larger follow-up; the sequential-fetch + off-isolate-decode combination is the smallest correct fix that removes the six-way coexistence and the UI stall.
- **Blast radius:** getXtreamHttpData is called by fetchXtreamAccountInfo (line 423), checkXtreamAuth (line 475), fetchXtreamMaxConnections (line 398), getEpisodes (line 741), and the fix321 retryType Future.wait (line 168) and _fetchVodPerCategory. Moving decode into Isolate.run affects ALL of them — verify each still gets the decoded object (they do; the return type is unchanged `dynamic`). The retry path at line 168 also does Future.wait of 2 fetches; the per-type refactor should keep the retry consistent. Rewriting the results[0..5] gate touches the failCount/keepMediaTypes decision block that findings 189 and 345 also touch — coordinate.
- **Acceptance:** DEVICE-ONLY for the memory/stall claim: cannot be proven from source or unit test. MANUAL/DEVICE: on a 2 GB Android TV box (onn 4K or Shield) add a 400k+-channel Xtream source and observe (a) no low-memory OS kill during refresh, (b) Android Studio Profiler peak Dart heap during refresh drops versus baseline, (c) UI stays responsive (progress dialog animates) during the decode phase. STATIC fallback for the off-isolate decode: add test/xtream_decode_offisolate_test.dart asserting getXtreamHttpData source text contains `Isolate.run` (or `compute(`) wrapping `jsonDecode`, and that getXtream no longer contains a single `Future.wait([` fetching all six actions (grep the three action constants are no longer all in one Future.wait).
- **Notes:** Largest edit; do LAST. The per-type sequential rewrite must preserve fix321 (wipe spliced before contentStatements) and fix322 (failCount reconcile) semantics exactly.

#### 63. [P2] xtream.dart:~189 — Transient fetch failure for a content type with lastCount null/0 skips the preserve guard and wipes that type'

- **Anchor:** getXtream() — the fix321 `if (wipe)` retry block, first `XtreamRefreshLogic.shouldRetryType(count: liveCount, lastCount: source.lastLiveCount)` call and the two like it for movie/series
- **Current code:**
```dart
    if (XtreamRefreshLogic.shouldRetryType(
        count: liveCount, lastCount: source.lastLiveCount)) {
      liveCount = await retryType(
          getLiveStreams, getLiveStreamCategories, MediaType.livestream);
      if (liveCount == 0) {
        keepMediaTypes.add(MediaType.livestream.index);
```
- **Fix:** The bug: shouldRetryType gates on `(lastCount ?? 0) > 0`, so a type whose last count is NULL/0 never retries AND never gets added to keepMediaTypes, so wipeSource deletes its existing rows on a transient failure. Fix by making the keep/preserve decision depend on whether rows ACTUALLY EXIST in the DB, not on the recorded count. Steps: (1) Add a new Sql helper `static Future<bool> sourceHasMediaType(int sourceId, int mediaType)` in sql.dart returning `SELECT EXISTS(SELECT 1 FROM channels WHERE source_id=? AND media_type=? LIMIT 1)` as a bool. (2) In getXtream, for each of the three types, when the fresh fetch produced 0 rows (count==0) — regardless of lastCount — call `await Sql.sourceHasMediaType(source.id!, MediaType.X.index)`; if true, add that type's index to keepMediaTypes (preserve existing rows) instead of letting the wipe delete them. Keep the existing shouldRetryType-driven single retry as-is for the case where lastCount>0 (it still helps recover), but the keepMediaTypes add must be driven by the EXISTS check so NULL/0 lastCount sources are also protected. This makes the preserve path independent of the possibly-stale lastCount column that line 285-289 cements to 0.
- **Blast radius:** Adds a read query per empty content type (max 3 tiny EXISTS reads per refresh on the read pool — negligible). keepMediaTypes flows into Sql.wipeSource (line 231), the fix322 shouldThrowAllFailed decision (line 242), and the count-persistence block (lines 282-289) which already skips writing counts for kept types — that behavior stays correct. Touches sql.dart (new helper) — a SECOND FILE. Coordinate with finding 345: if 345 makes a non-List response count as a failure (results null), the count==0 path here becomes cleaner because a genuine empty is distinguishable from a failed fetch.
- **Acceptance:** Add test/xtream_preserve_on_transient_fail_test.dart. Unit-test the pure decision if extracted, else a sqlite_async in-memory DB test: seed a source with movie rows (one favorite) and lastMovieCount=NULL; simulate movieCount=0 (fetch failure); assert that after the wipe-decision, MediaType.movie.index is in keepMediaTypes AND after commit the movie favorite row still exists (`SELECT COUNT(*) FROM channels WHERE source_id=? AND media_type=? AND favorite=1` == 1). Assert Sql.sourceHasMediaType returns true for a source with rows and false for none.
- **Notes:** Root cause is the lastCount-based gate, not the retry itself. The EXISTS check is authoritative over the drift-prone lastCount column.

#### 64. [P2] xtream.dart:~324 — Wipe+reinsert is not atomic past ~500 closures: process death mid-commit leaves a silent partial catalog and t · CONFIRMED

- **Anchor:** getXtream() — `await Sql.updateSource(source);` (line ~306) preceding the commit, and the `await Sql.commitWriteBatched(statements, ...)` inside `Sql.withSuspendedFtsTriggers` near the end of getXtream
- **Current code:**
```dart
    await Sql.updateSource(source);
  }
```
- **Fix:** Two minimal, independent changes that together make an interrupted refresh non-destructive. (1) MOVE updateSource AFTER a successful commit: cut the `await Sql.updateSource(source);` call (and only that call — leave the field assignments source.lastLiveCount=... in place before the commit) out of the `if (source.id != null)` block and re-issue it immediately AFTER `swCommit.stop();` at the end of getXtream, still guarded by `if (source.id != null)`. This ensures lastLiveCount/lastMovieCount/lastSeriesCount are only persisted once the wipe+inserts+restorePreserve have all committed, so a crash mid-commit leaves the OLD counts and fix321/shouldRetryType still sees lastCount>0 on the retry (preserve path fires). NOTE: keep the `Sql.setSourceEnabled(false, ...)` expiry write where it is (line 304) — that is a deliberate separate concern. (2) SNAPSHOT preserve across the retry-pair: preserve is captured fresh at line 50 on every getXtream call, so a retry after a partial commit re-captures from the already-damaged rows and loses favorites. The cleanest fix without a schema change: leave preserve capture here but change the retry driver in utils.dart:239-262 so the SAME getXtream attempt's preserve cannot be lost — because moving updateSource (change 1) keeps lastCount>0, the fix189/321 EXISTS-preserve path already protects the rows on the retry. Therefore change (1) is the required fix; change (2) reduces to: confirm (via change 1) that after an interrupted commit the next attempt's getChannelsPreserve still finds the favorites (they were never wiped because the wipe+insert batch that ran did not commit favorite-destroying state without the restore). Do NOT introduce a generation/shadow column in this change — that is a larger follow-up; document it as a known residual risk in the log message.
- **Blast radius:** updateSource writes maxConnections/expDate/status/counts. Moving it after the commit means those are not persisted if the commit throws — that is the DESIRED behavior (don't record success for a failed write). The expiry auto-disable path (setSourceEnabled at 304) stays before the commit and is unaffected. utils.dart retry loop (239-262) calls the whole pipeline again on throw — with change (1) the counts are still old so preserve is protected. commitWriteBatched splitting at importBatchSize=500 (sql.dart:70) is the underlying non-atomicity and is NOT changed here (a single transaction over 450k closures is itself infeasible on 2 GB). SECOND FILE: none required for change (1); a full shadow-generation fix would touch sql.dart schema + wipeSource.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC + unit. STATIC: grep getXtream to assert `Sql.updateSource(source)` now appears AFTER `swCommit.stop()` (i.e. after the commitWriteBatched call), not before it. Unit (test/xtream_updatesource_after_commit_test.dart): with an in-memory DB, make commitWriteBatched throw partway (inject a failing closure); assert source.lastLiveCount in the DB is UNCHANGED (still the prior value, not the new fetched count) after the throw. The full process-death atomicity guarantee CANNOT be proven without killing the process mid-commit on a device — note that in the test as a MANUAL/DEVICE caveat: on a 2GB box, kill the app during a >500k-row refresh commit and confirm the next launch's refresh restores favorites.
- **Notes:** The verdict is CONFIRMED. The single load-bearing edit is moving updateSource after the commit; everything else is defense-in-depth already provided by fix189.

#### 65. [P2] xtream.dart:~345 — processJsonList converts an HTTP-200 error/HTML body into an empty list, indistinguishable from a legitimately

- **Anchor:** top-level `processJsonList<T>` function — the `if (jsonData is! List) return [];` line
- **Current code:**
```dart
  if (jsonData is! List) return [];
  return jsonData
      .map((json) => fromJson(json as Map<String, dynamic>))
      .toList();
```
- **Fix:** Make a non-List response a FETCH FAILURE, not a valid empty type. Because getWithRetry already returns null for non-200 (http_client.dart:38), the only way a non-List reaches here is an HTTP-200 body that is a Map/error object. Change processJsonList to THROW on a non-List so the existing `try { ... } catch (e) { failCount++; }` blocks in getXtream (lines 84-97, 102-129, 135-148) count it as a failure: replace the snippet's first line with:
  if (jsonData is! List) {
    // fix: an HTTP-200 non-array body (auth error object, HTML, {user_info:{auth:0}})
    // is a provider failure, NOT an empty content type. Log the shape and throw
    // so the caller's catch increments failCount and the preserve/retry path runs.
    AppLog.warn('Xtream.processJsonList: expected a JSON array but got '
        '${jsonData.runtimeType}${jsonData is Map ? ' keys=' + jsonData.keys.take(5).toString() : ''}');
    throw const FormatException('Xtream response was not a JSON array');
  }
Additionally, the fix321 retryType path (line 174) calls processJsonList inside its own try/catch and returns 0 on throw — that is correct (a non-List retry counts as still-failed → preserve). Requires `import 'package:open_tv/backend/app_logger.dart';` which is already present (line 4). SEPARATE, OPTIONAL sub-point about user_info.auth==0: do NOT add auth-shape inspection inside processJsonList (it only receives the stream/category arrays, never the auth object); auth detection belongs in getXtreamHttpData or the account-info path and is out of scope for this minimal fix — a non-List simply becomes a failure, which is the correct outcome for auth==0 too.
- **Blast radius:** processJsonList is called from getXtream lines 85, 91, 103, 104, 136, 142 and retryType lines 174, 179, and possibly _fetchVodPerCategory — all are already inside try/catch that increments failCount or returns 0, so throwing is safe. This CHANGES behavior: a provider that genuinely returns a non-array for an empty type will now count as a failure and (via fix189/321) preserve prior rows or retry — desired. Verify no caller uses processJsonList outside a try/catch (grep confirms all in-file uses are guarded). Coordinate with finding 189: this throw is what lets 189 distinguish failure from empty.
- **Acceptance:** Add test/xtream_process_json_list_test.dart: (1) `expect(() => processJsonList({'user_info': {'auth': 0}}, XtreamStream.fromJson), throwsA(isA<FormatException>()))`; (2) `expect(processJsonList([], XtreamStream.fromJson), isEmpty)` — genuine empty array still returns []; (3) `expect(() => processJsonList('<html>...', XtreamStream.fromJson), throwsFormatException)`.
- **Notes:** Genuine empty array MUST still return [] (a provider with zero series is valid). Only non-List throws.

#### 66. [P3] xtream.dart:~378 — Debug raw-response dumps write full provider catalogs (hundreds of MB) to the app dir on every refresh and are

- **Anchor:** getXtreamHttpData() — the `if (AppLog.enabled)` block that writes `File('$dir/xtream_dump_${source.id}_$safeAction.json')` via `f.writeAsString(response.body)`
- **Current code:**
```dart
        final f = File('$dir/xtream_dump_${source.id}_$safeAction.json');
        await f.writeAsString(response.body);
        AppLog.info('Xtream: dumped raw response action="$action" '
            'source=${source.id} bytes=${response.body.length} to ${f.path}');
```
- **Fix:** Cap the dump to the first N KB (enough to diagnose the JSON shape). Introduce `const int _kMaxDumpBytes = 256 * 1024;` near the top of the file (with the other consts around line 24) and change the write to a truncated substring:
        final body = response.body;
        final dump = body.length > _kMaxDumpBytes
            ? body.substring(0, _kMaxDumpBytes) + '\n/*…truncated ${body.length - _kMaxDumpBytes} bytes…*/'
            : body;
        final f = File('$dir/xtream_dump_${source.id}_$safeAction.json');
        await f.writeAsString(dump);
        AppLog.info('Xtream: dumped raw response action="$action" '
            'source=${source.id} bytes=${body.length} (capped to ${dump.length}) to ${f.path}');
This keeps format diagnosis while bounding disk to ~256 KB per action. (Decision: cap rather than delete-on-disable, because the files are keyed by source+action so they self-overwrite and 256KB * ~7 actions * few sources is trivial; a startup purge is a nice-to-have but the cap alone removes the ~1 GB risk with a one-site change.)
- **Blast radius:** Only affects the debug-dump path (gated on AppLog.enabled). The truncated file is no longer valid JSON for replay-in-sandbox (the fix222 use case) for large bodies — acceptable tradeoff for a P3 debug aid; note in the log line that the dump is capped so anyone using it for replay knows. No callers depend on the dump file.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC: grep getXtreamHttpData asserts the write no longer passes `response.body` directly to writeAsString and that `_kMaxDumpBytes` / a substring cap is present. MANUAL/DEVICE (optional): enable debug logging, refresh a large source, confirm each xtream_dump_*.json in the app dir is <= ~256 KB.
- **Notes:** Minimal one-site cap; do not add a purge path in this change unless the implementer wants the extra scope.

#### 70. [P1] tv_guide_view.dart:~449 — Guide PopScope + shell ConfirmExitScope both fire on one Back: two quick Backs from channels rail exit the app

- **Anchor:** TvGuideView.build() PopScope with `canPop: _railMode != RailMode.channels` and `onPopInvokedWithResult` calling `_swapToCategories()`; cross-file _ConfirmExitScopeState.build() in lib/confirm_exit_scope.dart with `final atRoot = !Navigator.of(context).canPop();`
- **Current code:**
```dart
    return PopScope(
      canPop: _railMode != RailMode.channels,
      onPopInvokedWithResult: (didPop, result) {
        if (didPop) return;
        _swapToCategories();
      },
```
- **Fix:** DECISION: keep the guide's PopScope but make ConfirmExitScope NOT arm when a nested PopScope already consumed the Back. Add a per-frame consumed flag to ConfirmExitScope. Step 1 — in lib/confirm_exit_scope.dart, add a static `static bool _popConsumedThisFrame = false;` and a public static method `static void notePopConsumed() { _popConsumedThisFrame = true; WidgetsBinding.instance.addPostFrameCallback((_) => _popConsumedThisFrame = false); }`. Step 2 — in _ConfirmExitScopeState.build's `onPopInvokedWithResult`, at the very top add `if (didPop) return;` (already there) then `if (ConfirmExitScope._popConsumedThisFrame) return;` BEFORE arming/showing the snackbar. Step 3 — in tv_guide_view.dart change the guide's onPopInvokedWithResult body to: `if (didPop) return; ConfirmExitScope.notePopConsumed(); _swapToCategories();` and add `import 'package:open_tv/confirm_exit_scope.dart';` at the top of tv_guide_view.dart. Rationale: because Flutter invokes every registered PopEntry's callback on a single blocked pop within the same frame, the guide's callback runs and sets the flag; the shell's ConfirmExitScope callback (also this frame) sees it set and skips arming — so a first Back only collapses the rail and does NOT arm the 2s exit window, and does NOT show 'Press Back again to exit'. The post-frame callback clears the flag so a genuine root Back in categories mode still arms normally.
- **Blast radius:** Touches TWO files: lib/tv/tv_guide_view.dart (build PopScope + new import) and lib/confirm_exit_scope.dart (new static flag + guard). ConfirmExitScope also wraps Home and SettingsView (phone) per its doc comment — the new guard is inert there because no other nested PopScope calls notePopConsumed(), so phone confirm-to-exit is unchanged. Any future nested PopScope that wants to suppress the exit hint on a consumed Back must also call notePopConsumed().
- **Acceptance:** MANUAL/DEVICE (onn 4K / any Android TV, D-pad only): open Live tab, OK into a category (channels mode), press Back once — rail returns to categories AND no 'Press Back again to exit' snackbar appears AND app does not exit; immediately press Back again within 2s — first press arms and shows the hint (categories mode is at root), second press exits. Also STATIC: `grep -n notePopConsumed lib/confirm_exit_scope.dart lib/tv/tv_guide_view.dart` shows the setter in the guide and the guard in the scope.

```
    final cats = _groups.where((g) => g.id != null).toList();
    return ListView.builder(
      key: const ValueKey('rail-categories'),
      padding: const EdgeInsets.symmetric(vertical: 8),
      itemCount: cats.length + 1,
```

#### 75. [P2] tv_guide_view.dart:~1074 — EPG grid programme blocks are focusable InkWells despite the 'passive grid' design — D-pad focus wanders into 

- **Anchor:** TvGuideView._block() `child: InkWell(\n            onTap: () => _play(ch),` inside the `Material(...)` positioned programme block (comment at _gridRow says 'passive timeline row (no name column, no focus)')
- **Current code:**

```dart
            onTap: () => _play(ch),
            borderRadius: BorderRadius.circular(4),
```
- **Fix:** Make the programme block non-focusable so it stays passive on TV while keeping onTap for touch builds. Wrap the InkWell in `ExcludeFocus`. Change the block child from `child: InkWell(onTap: () => _play(ch), borderRadius: ...)` to `child: ExcludeFocus(child: InkWell(onTap: () => _play(ch), borderRadius: BorderRadius.circular(4), child: ...))` — i.e. wrap the existing InkWell (and its child) in `ExcludeFocus(child: <InkWell>)`. ExcludeFocus removes the whole subtree from focus traversal, so D-pad RIGHT from a rail channel no longer lands inside the grid, the one-way _syncGridToRail mirror stays authoritative, and _onChannelFocused keeps driving the preview from the rail only. onTap remains functional for touchscreens (a tap does not require focus). Do NOT use `canRequestFocus:false` on the InkWell alone — the enclosing Material/Positioned could still create focusable descendants; ExcludeFocus is the robust choice. `ExcludeFocus` is in the already-imported `package:flutter/material.dart`.
- **Blast radius:** In-file. On touch builds the block is still tappable. If any future feature wants a focusable grid (e.g. programme details on TV), ExcludeFocus would block it — acceptable given the stated passive-grid design (comment at _gridRow line ~1019). No second file. Verify no other code calls FocusScope into a grid block.
- **Acceptance:** MANUAL/DEVICE (onn 4K, D-pad): open a category (channels mode), focus a channel in the rail, press RIGHT repeatedly — focus stays in the rail / does not enter the EPG grid, the highlighted channel row and its rail tile stay aligned. If other favorite writers bypass favoriteChannel, they must also bump. ### `lib/backend/m3u.dart`  — 7 finding(s) [P1×4 P2×1 P3×2]

**File notes:** Apply BOTTOM-UP so earlier edits don't shift the anchors of later ones, and because several edits are in the same functions. Recommended order: (1) F7 getName else-branch #-filter [~line 105]; then work upward — (2) F3 downloadM3U temp-file cleanup + (4) F4 body-timeout: BOTH live in downloadM3U/processM3UUrl (~lines 235-281) and MUST be co-designed (see below); (5) F5 credential redaction is in a SEPARATE file (app_logger.dart) — independent, do it anytime; (6) F6 nameRegexAlt (line 17) is independent; (7) F2 bulk-insert restructures the parse loop / commitChannel (lines 61-159); (8) F1 wipe-safety restructures processM3U's top (lines 43-140) and MUST be layered ON TOP of the F2 rewrite because F1 needs the parsed channel count/buffer that F2 introduces.

CRITICAL COUPLING: F1 (wipe-before-parse) and F2 (bulk buffering) and F4 (truncation flag) all rewrite the SAME processM3U body. Implement them as ONE coordinated rewrite of processM3U, not three independent diffs, or they will conflict. Concretely: F2 introduces a `final buffer = <Channel>[]` + `flush()` that emits `Sql.insertChannelsBulk` closures into `batch`; F1 then (a) removes the standalone `await Sql.commitWrite([Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)]...)` at line 54 and instead PREPENDS `Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)` to the FIRST content commit only after a plausible non-zero count is confirmed (mirror xtream.dart:229-233 which appends wipeSource in front of contentStatements in the same transaction); (F4) sets a `truncated` bool that suppresses updateSource/wipe when the download didn't reach EOF.

SHARED HELPERS/IMPORTS already present: `Sql.insertChannelsBulk` (sql.dart:748, does NOT read last_insert_rowid), `bulkInsertRows`=1000 (sql.dart:33), `importBatchSize`=500 (already imported at m3u.dart:5), `Sql.wipeSource(sourceId, {keepMediaTypes})` (sql.dart:2096). For F3 you need `import 'package:path/path.dart'` only if you sweep the dir; simplest cleanup uses `File(path).delete()` (dart:io already imported). No new deps required for any finding.

DECISION on F1 vs F2 count gate: use the count of PARSED channels (buffer/channelCount) compared to `source.lastLiveCount`. Reuse the xtream threshold helper if desired but a simple rule is specified per-finding.

#### 78. [P1] m3u.dart:~54 — M3U refresh wipes catalog before parsing — transient/empty/malformed download permanently destroys catalog + f · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** processM3U — the standalone wipe commit: grep `Sql.commitWrite([Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)]`
- **Current code:**
```dart
    await Sql.commitWrite([Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)], memory: memory);
  }

  var file = File(
    path!,
  ).openRead().transform(utf8.decoder).transform(const LineSplitter());
```
- **Fix:** Do NOT wipe up front. Mirror the Xtream deferred-wipe pattern (xtream.dart:229-233): parse the whole playlist into insert closures FIRST, then splice `Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)` in front of those closures in the SAME transaction only if the parse produced a plausible count. Concretely: (1) Delete the `await Sql.commitWrite([Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)], memory: memory);` line at ~54 (keep the `preserve = await Sql.getChannelsPreserve(sourceId);` capture above it). (2) Change the utf8 decode to tolerate bad bytes: `.transform(utf8.decoder)` becomes `.transform(const Utf8Decoder(allowMalformed: true))`. (3) Accumulate all channel insert closures into `batch` WITHOUT committing during the loop when `wipe==true` (or into a separate `contentStatements` list) so nothing is written until the final count is known — for a 450k list this must stay streamed, so instead keep a running `channelCount` and DEFER only the wipe, not the inserts: build the first commit batch, and before committing the FIRST batch prepend `Sql.wipeSource(sourceId)` to it, but ONLY after guarding: if `channelCount==0` at end-of-parse, skip wipe+updateSource entirely and return (log a warning), leaving the old catalog intact; and if `source.lastLiveCount != null && source.lastLiveCount! > 100 && channelCount < (source.lastLiveCount! ~/ 5)` (parsed <20% of prior), skip the wipe/updateSource and log 'M3U: refusing to replace N prior channels with M (<20%) — keeping existing catalog'. RECOMMENDED concrete shape: parse fully into `List<Channel>` buffers emitting bulk closures into a local `contentStatements` list (combine with F2); after the loop, if the count gate passes, do `if (wipe) contentStatements.insert(0, Sql.wipeSource(sourceId));` then `await Sql.commitWriteBatched(contentStatements, ...)` then the tail (updateGroups + restorePreserve). This keeps wipe+insert atomic so a mid-parse throw rolls back the wipe. Because F4 also gates on a `truncated` flag, wire that flag into the same 'skip wipe/updateSource' guard.
- **Blast radius:** processM3U is called by processM3UUrl (local-file path passes path directly) and by refresh flows in utils.dart (refreshSource / refreshAllSources fix611 retry). Deferring the wipe changes memory usage: for a 450k list the insert closures already stream in batches of 500 today, so keep streaming — do NOT hold all 450k Channel objects if avoidable; the count gate only needs a running counter, not the full list. restorePreserve (tail) already runs after; unaffected. No second file required, but this rewrite must be coordinated with F2 (bulk) and F4 (truncation) which touch the same function body. Verify commitWriteBatched wraps each batch in its own transaction (sql.dart:70) — if wipe is only prepended to batch #1, batches 2..N commit in separate transactions, so a throw after batch #1 leaves a partial catalog; acceptable (better than total loss) but note it.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC + TEST: add unit test `processM3U_emptyParseKeepsCatalog` — feed a local temp file containing zero valid EXTINF entries (e.g. only an HTML error body) to processM3U with wipe=true and a source whose lastLiveCount=1000; assert wipeSource closure was NOT committed and updateSource was NOT called (spy on Sql). Add `processM3U_malformedUtf8DoesNotThrow` — file with an invalid UTF-8 byte mid-stream parses without throwing and yields the surrounding valid channels. Add `processM3U_partialParseBelowThresholdKeepsCatalog` — 100 parsed vs lastLiveCount=1000 keeps old catalog. DEVICE (onn 4K Plus): point an m3uUrl source at a URL returning HTTP-200 HTML; refresh; confirm existing channels + favorites remain.

#### 79. [P1] m3u.dart:~155 — M3U import does one INSERT + last_insert_rowid per channel (no bulk) — 450k rows = ~900k round-trips

- **Anchor:** commitChannel — grep `statements.add(Sql.insertChannel(channel));`
- **Current code:**
```dart
  statements.add(Sql.insertChannel(channel));
  if (headers != null) {
    statements.add(Sql.insertChannelHeaders(headers));
  }
```
- **Fix:** Switch the common path to `Sql.insertChannelsBulk` (sql.dart:748, 1000 rows/statement, no rowid read) and keep `Sql.insertChannel` (which sets memory['lastChannelId'] via last_insert_rowid, sql.dart:204) ONLY for the rare channel that carries EXTVLCOPT headers (needs the rowid for insertChannelHeaders). Concretely, restructure processM3U's parse loop to buffer plain channels the way processXtream does (xtream.dart:619-652): add `final buffer = <Channel>[];` and a `void flushChannels(){ if(buffer.isEmpty) return; batch.add(Sql.insertChannelsBulk(List<Channel>.from(buffer))); buffer.clear(); }`. In commitChannel, replace the body after the divider check with: if `headers != null` keep the current pair (`statements.add(Sql.insertChannel(channel)); statements.add(Sql.insertChannelHeaders(headers));`) so the header row still resolves the rowid; else push `channel` into the shared buffer and call `flushChannels()` when `buffer.length >= bulkInsertRows`. Since commitChannel currently receives `statements` (the batch list) not the buffer, pass the buffer+flush in (simplest: inline the buffering into the loop at m3u.dart:80-112 rather than in commitChannel, calling getChannelFromLines directly and checking channel.isDivider there, so the buffer and `batch` are both in scope). Ensure `flushChannels()` is called before each `flushBatch()` and once after the loop so ordering (provider_order) and header-row rowid dependencies stay correct. Import: none new (insertChannelsBulk and bulkInsertRows already exported from sql.dart).
- **Blast radius:** Changes provider_order sequencing only if buffering reorders — it must NOT: flush the bulk buffer BEFORE emitting any insertChannel(header) closure so the header channel's rowid is the immediately-preceding INSERT. Interacts directly with F1 (the same closures feed the deferred-wipe transaction) — implement together. insertChannelsBulk uses the same ON CONFLICT upsert key as insertChannel (sql.dart:745-746) so semantics match. commitWriteBatched batches at importBatchSize=500 closures/tx; with bulk closures each closure is 1000 rows, so a 500-closure batch = 500k rows in one transaction — that may be too large for a 2GB box. Reduce the per-batch flush: call flushBatch() when `batch.length >= 1` bulk closure OR keep importBatchSize but be aware each tx now holds up to 500 bulk statements. RECOMMENDED: after adding a bulk closure, `if (batch.isNotEmpty) await flushBatch();` so each 1000-row bulk statement commits promptly (matches xtream cadence). No second file.
- **Acceptance:** TEST `processM3U_usesBulkInsertForPlainChannels`: feed a temp file with 2500 plain EXTINF+URL pairs and 1 EXTVLCOPT-bearing entry; spy Sql to assert insertChannelsBulk was used (>=3 bulk closures for 2500 rows) and insertChannel was called exactly once (for the header-bearing channel). Assert total rows inserted == 2501 and provider_order is contiguous 0..2500 in insertion order. Cannot fully prove 450k timing without a device + large playlist.

#### 80. [P1] m3u.dart:~266 — Downloaded M3U temp files never deleted — each m3uUrl refresh leaks a unique multi-MB file

- **Anchor:** downloadM3U — grep `final path = await Utils.getTempPath("get_$unique.m3u");`
- **Current code:**
```dart

    await processM3U(source, wipe, path, onProgress);
  } catch (e) {
    AppLog.warn('M3U: download failed source="${source.name}" error=$e');
    rethrow;
  }
```
- **Fix:** Delete the downloaded temp file in a `finally` in processM3UUrl so it is removed on both success and failure (but only the file downloaded here — NOT a caller-supplied local path). Rewrite processM3UUrl's try/catch to: `String? path; try { path = await downloadM3U(source.url!); await processM3U(source, wipe, path, onProgress); } catch (e) { AppLog.warn(...); rethrow; } finally { if (path != null) { try { final f = File(path); if (await f.exists()) await f.delete(); } catch (e) { AppLog.warn('M3U: temp cleanup failed path="$path" error=$e'); } } }`. Additionally, add a best-effort sweep of stale leaked files at the START of downloadM3U (before writing the new one): list the temp dir and delete any `get_*.m3u` (they are always this function's output). Concretely, after computing the temp dir, `final tempDir = Directory(await Utils.getTempPath('.')).parent;` is awkward — instead add a small helper in downloadM3U: `final dir = File(path).parent; try { await for (final e in dir.list()) { if (e is File && e.path.split('/').last.startsWith('get_') && e.path.endsWith('.m3u') && e.path != path) { try { await e.delete(); } catch (_) {} } } } catch (_) {}` placed right after `final path = await Utils.getTempPath(...)` and before opening the sink. dart:io File/Directory already imported.
- **Blast radius:** processM3U is ALSO called directly with a local file path (local-file source, path passed by a non-URL caller) — that path must NOT be deleted, which is why the delete lives in processM3UUrl (only the downloaded file) not in processM3U. The startup sweep only matches `get_*.m3u` (this function's naming) so it won't touch user files. getTempPath is used ONLY here (utils.dart:24), so the sweep is safe app-wide. Note SettingsIo.purgeStaleExportArtifacts operates on getTemporaryDirectory() (a DIFFERENT dir) — no overlap. No second file needed.
- **Acceptance:** TEST `processM3UUrl_deletesTempOnSuccess` and `_deletesTempOnFailure`: stub downloadM3U to write a temp file, run processM3UUrl (success + throwing processM3U), assert the file no longer exists in both cases. #### 81. [P1] m3u.dart:~271 — M3U body-stream stall closes sink cleanly → truncated playlist persisted as a complete refresh · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** downloadM3U — grep `onTimeout: (sink) => sink.close()`
- **Current code:**
```dart
  await for (var chunk in response.stream.timeout(
    const Duration(seconds: 60),
    onTimeout: (sink) => sink.close(),
  )) {
    sink.add(chunk);
  }
  await sink.close();
  final length = await file.length();
  if (length == 0) {
    throw Exception('Downloaded M3U file is empty');
  }
  return path;
```
- **Fix:** On the idle timeout, EMIT AN ERROR into the stream instead of closing it cleanly, so the `await for` throws and propagates up through processM3UUrl's catch/rethrow (m3u.dart:245-248), which (after F1) leaves the old catalog intact. Change the timeout handler from `onTimeout: (sink) => sink.close()` (note: the `sink` param here is an EventSink for the transformed stream, shadowing the file sink — closing it silently ends the loop) to `onTimeout: (eventSink) => eventSink.addError(Exception('M3U download stalled: no data for 60s'))`. Rename the timeout callback param to `eventSink` to avoid confusion with the file `sink`. After adding the error, the `await for` throws; ensure the partially-written file sink is closed and deleted before the exception escapes: wrap the download in try/finally within downloadM3U — `try { await for (...) { sink.add(chunk); } } finally { await sink.close(); }` then on the thrown path let it propagate (the F3 finally in processM3UUrl deletes the temp file). Do NOT keep the `length==0` check as the only guard — a stall after some bytes yields length>0 today; erroring on timeout is the fix.
- **Blast radius:** Any slow-but-legitimate provider that legitimately pauses >60s mid-body will now fail the refresh instead of silently truncating — this is the correct trade-off (better a failed refresh that keeps the old catalog than a silent partial replace). Couples with F1 (the throw must reach a state where the wipe has NOT been committed — guaranteed once F1 defers the wipe) and F3 (finally deletes the partial file). If F1 is NOT yet applied, this finding alone still prevents persisting a truncated count because processM3U will throw before reaching updateSource — but the pre-F1 wipe at line 54 would already have destroyed the catalog, so F1 MUST land with or before F4. No second file.
- **Acceptance:** TEST `downloadM3U_throwsOnBodyTimeout`: back the stream with a controller that emits a few chunks then never completes; drive the 60s timeout (inject a shortened duration or use fakeAsync) and assert downloadM3U throws with the 'stalled' message and the partial temp file is deleted. Integration: assert processM3UUrl rethrows and (with F1) the prior catalog/count is unchanged. Cannot fully reproduce the real 60s network stall without a device or a controllable mock origin — use fakeAsync/StreamController in the unit test.

#### 82. [P2] m3u.dart:~240 — m3uUrl credentials in query string leak into exportable debug log (redaction only covers Xtream username/passw

- **Anchor:** AppLogger.setSourceSecrets (app_logger.dart) — grep `if (u.trim().isNotEmpty) out.add(MapEntry(u, '<${tag}_USER>'));`

```dart
      final u = s.username ?? '';
      final p = s.password ?? '';
      if (u.trim().isNotEmpty) out.add(MapEntry(u, '<${tag}_USER>'));
      if (p.trim().isNotEmpty) out.add(MapEntry(p, '<${tag}_PASS>'));
```
- **Fix:** SECOND FILE: edit lib/backend/app_logger.dart, not m3u.dart. In setSourceSecrets, after the existing username/password adds, also extract credential-bearing query params from every source URL (covers m3uUrl `?username=U&password=P` form where s.username/s.password are null). The existing longest-first sort at app_logger.dart:161 already ensures the credential literal is redacted before shorter substrings. This makes the m3uUrl `url="..."` line logged at m3u.dart:240 redact to `<TAG_HOST>/get.php?username=<TAG_CRED>&password=<TAG_CRED>`.
- **Blast radius:** setSourceSecrets is the single redaction-table builder consumed by _redactSecrets (app_logger.dart:183) for ALL log output, so this also protects stream_scanner.dart:104-106 and any other full-URL log line. STATIC: grep the exported log after a real m3uUrl refresh for the known password literal — must be absent.

#### 83. [P3] m3u.dart:~17 — M3U fallback name extraction truncates channel names containing commas (anchors to LAST comma)

- **Anchor:** top-level regex — grep `final nameRegexAlt = RegExp(r',([^,\n\r\t]*)$');`
- **Current code:**
```dart
final nameRegexAlt = RegExp(r',([^,\n\r\t]*)$');
```
- **Fix:** The display name is everything after the FIRST comma following the attribute list, not after the last comma. Replace the regex so it captures from the first comma to end-of-line: `final nameRegexAlt = RegExp(r',(.+)$');`. This greedily takes the remainder after the first comma (RegExp.firstMatch finds the leftmost match, so `,` binds to the first comma; `(.+)$` then grabs the rest including subsequent commas). For `#EXTINF:-1 tvg-id="" group-title="Docs",Cosmos, A Spacetime Odyssey` this yields `Cosmos, A Spacetime Odyssey`. getName (m3u.dart:203-214) then `.trim()`s it. Note: attribute values are quoted and matched by the other regexes ([^"]*) so commas inside attributes don't interfere with those; the concern is only the trailing display title. Keep the `\n\r\t` exclusion unnecessary since LineSplitter already strips line breaks — `,(.+)$` is sufficient. If a defensive trim of a leading/trailing quote is desired it can be added in getName, but not required.
- **Blast radius:** getName is used for EVERY channel lacking tvg-name. Correcting truncation changes the imported `name` for comma-titled channels, which is the key used by favorites preservation (sql.dart:2470 matches on name) and EPG name-matching — this is a FIX (previously matched on the wrong truncated string) but means on first refresh after the change, a favorite previously stored under the truncated name won't match the now-correct name and could be lost once. Low incidence. Ordinary (no-comma) titles: `,(.+)$` still matches the same single-token tail, unchanged. No second file.
- **Acceptance:** TEST `getName_returnsFullTitleWithCommas`: assert getName('#EXTINF:-1 tvg-id="" group-title="Docs",Cosmos, A Spacetime Odyssey') == 'Cosmos, A Spacetime Odyssey'.       // buffering=true fired during open always arrived first and defeated
