```dart
      SELECT * FROM channels$hint
      WHERE source_id = ?
```
- **Fix:** Same catch-and-retry-without-hint pattern as finding 1107 — the foreground refresh (different isolate) can drop idx_epg_unmatched between this isolate's _indexExists check and the getAll. Keep the _indexExists gate; wrap the execution so a mid-flight drop degrades to the unhinted (planner-chosen) query instead of a hard crash that aborts the source's match. Build both strings and route through the shared _getAllHinted helper defined for finding 1107:
```
    final rows = await _getAllHinted(
      db,
      'SELECT * FROM channels INDEXED BY idx_epg_unmatched'
      ' WHERE source_id = ? AND media_type = 0'
      ' AND epg_manual_override IS NULL AND epg_channel_id IS NULL',
      'SELECT * FROM channels'
      ' WHERE source_id = ? AND media_type = 0'
      ' AND epg_manual_override IS NULL AND epg_channel_id IS NULL',
      [sourceId]);
```
If finding 1107 is NOT applied, inline an equivalent try/on SqliteException catch here that retries the unhinted string. If finding 3078's paging is applied, the paged variant must carry the same retry (add the hint+retry to getChannelsNeedingEpgMatchPage). Preserve the existing when-index-present optimization (only strip on the exception).
- **Blast radius:** getChannelsNeedingEpgMatch is on the incremental EPG-match path (forceAll=false), called from epg_service.dart in both foreground and background isolates. Depends on the shared _getAllHinted helper from finding 1107 (apply 1107 first, or inline the try/catch). The unhinted fallback is functionally identical (idx_epg_unmatched's partial predicate exactly equals the query WHERE). If finding 3078 restructures this into pages, coordinate so the hint+retry lives in the paged method.
- **Acceptance:** UNIT (add `needingEpgMatchRetriesUnhintedWhenIndexDropped` in test/backend/sql_epg_test.dart): seed unmatched channels, DROP idx_epg_unmatched, call getChannelsNeedingEpgMatch, assert it returns the correct unmatched rows without throwing. STATIC: grep shows getChannelsNeedingEpgMatch no longer calls bare `db.getAll` with the forced-hint string without a surrounding catch.
- **Notes:** verdict blank; cross-isolate ms-window race. Same SqliteException.message('no such index') caveat as finding 1107 — confirm the message text on the target build.

#### 137. [P3] sql.dart:~3134 — getAvailableEpgIds runs a correlated per-group subquery over the ~1.5M-row programmes table with no seekable p · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** getAvailableEpgIds(int sourceId) — grep 'AS sample_title' and the correlated `(SELECT title FROM programmes p2 WHERE p2.epg_channel_id = p.epg_channel_id AND p2.source_id = p.source_id ORDER BY start_utc DESC LIMIT 1)` (~line 3130-3144).
- **Current code:**
```dart
      SELECT epg_channel_id,
             (SELECT title FROM programmes p2
              WHERE p2.epg_channel_id = p.epg_channel_id
                AND p2.source_id = p.source_id
              ORDER BY start_utc DESC LIMIT 1) AS sample_title
      FROM programmes p
      WHERE source_id = ?
      GROUP BY epg_channel_id
      ORDER BY epg_channel_id ASC
```
- **Fix:** DECISION: replace the per-group correlated title lookup with a single grouped scan using a window-free MAX-join over the grouping the index already supports. Rewrite to group by epg_channel_id and pick a representative title via a correlated-free join on the max start_utc, or accept ANY title from the group (a display hint — exact recency is not required). Minimal correct rewrite (SQLite 3.25+ window function, available on all target runtimes per the file's own 3.39 discussion being about a different syntax — verify_first):
```
      SELECT epg_channel_id, title AS sample_title FROM (
        SELECT epg_channel_id, title,
               ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY epg_channel_id ORDER BY start_utc DESC) rn
        FROM programmes
        WHERE source_id = ?
      ) WHERE rn = 1
      ORDER BY epg_channel_id ASC
```
This reads the source's rows once (idx_programs_unique(source_id, epg_channel_id, start_utc) can serve the source_id seek + the partition/order), versus one extra probe per distinct epg_channel_id. If ROW_NUMBER support is a concern, the alternative is to drop recency entirely: `SELECT epg_channel_id, MIN(title) AS sample_title FROM programmes WHERE source_id = ? GROUP BY epg_channel_id ORDER BY epg_channel_id ASC` (a plain grouped aggregate the index groups directly) — sample_title is only a display hint, so an arbitrary title is acceptable. RECOMMEND the MIN(title) form for maximum SQLite-version safety; it is the smallest change and needs no window support.
- **Blast radius:** Only getAvailableEpgIds, called from the manual EPG channel-mapping dialog (epg_channel_mapping.dart:40) — a rare, user-initiated dialog, hence P3. The MIN(title) form changes which title is shown as the hint (arbitrary vs most-recent); confirm the dialog treats sample_title as a non-authoritative hint (it is labeled a display hint in the doc comment). No second file needed.
- **Acceptance:** UNIT (add `availableEpgIdsGroupsWithoutCorrelatedProbe` in test/backend/sql_epg_test.dart): seed multiple epg_channel_ids each with several programmes for one source, assert getAvailableEpgIds returns one row per distinct epg_channel_id, ascending, each with a non-empty sample_title. STATIC: grep shows no correlated `(SELECT title FROM programmes p2 ... ORDER BY start_utc DESC LIMIT 1)` subquery remains. DEVICE (perf, needs large EPG): open the manual mapping dialog on a large source and confirm it opens quickly rather than multi-second.
- **Notes:** verdict blank; lowest priority (rare dialog). If choosing the ROW_NUMBER form, confirm the bundled sqlite supports window functions (3.25+) on the oldest target Android before shipping — the MIN(title) fallback avoids that risk entirely.

### `lib/backend/epg_matcher.dart`  — 3 finding(s) [P2×2 P3×1]

**File notes:** All three findings live in one file, one static method (`matchWithReport`) plus its helpers. Apply in this order to avoid churn and offset drift:

Editing them separately would rewrite the same loop twice. Treat finding 3's `epgIdsLower` precompute as the shared substrate and finding 2's boundary check as operating on it.

#### 138. [P2] epg_matcher.dart:~79 — Tier 3/4 normalization collisions resolve last-wins with no ambiguity guard

- **Anchor:** EpgMatcher.matchWithReport, map-building loop: grep `byNormalizedName[norm] = epgId;` and `if (stripped != epgId) byStrippedId[stripped] = epgId;`; tier lookups grep `final tier3 = byNormalizedName[normName];` and `final tier4 = byStrippedId[strippedCh]`
- **Current code:**
```dart
      final norm = _normalize(displayName);
      byNormalizedName[norm] = epgId;
      // Also key by the EPG id itself (some feeds reuse names as IDs)
      byNormalizedName.putIfAbsent(_normalize(epgId), () => epgId);
```
- **Fix:** Detect collisions on `byNormalizedName` and `byStrippedId` and make tiers 3/4 skip ambiguous keys (consistent with the fuzzy-tier tie rule: better unmatched than wrong).

STEP A — declare two ambiguity sets next to the maps (just after `final byStrippedId = <String, String>{};`):
    final ambiguousNorms = <String>{};      // norm keys that map to >1 distinct epgId
    final ambiguousStripped = <String>{};   // stripped keys that map to >1 distinct epgId

STEP B — replace the plain overwrite `byNormalizedName[norm] = epgId;` with collision-aware insertion:
    final priorNorm = byNormalizedName[norm];
    if (priorNorm == null) {
      byNormalizedName[norm] = epgId;
    } else if (priorNorm != epgId) {
      ambiguousNorms.add(norm);
    }
Leave the `putIfAbsent(_normalize(epgId), ...)` line as-is (id-as-name is a weak signal; putIfAbsent already prefers the first/display-name key).

STEP C — replace `if (stripped != epgId) byStrippedId[stripped] = epgId;` with:
    if (stripped != epgId) {
      final priorStripped = byStrippedId[stripped];
      if (priorStripped == null) {
        byStrippedId[stripped] = epgId;
      } else if (priorStripped != epgId) {
        ambiguousStripped.add(stripped);
      }
    }

STEP D — guard tier 3: change `final tier3 = byNormalizedName[normName];` block so an ambiguous key does not match:
    final tier3 = ambiguousNorms.contains(normName) ? null : byNormalizedName[normName];

STEP E — guard tier 4: the current tier4 is `byStrippedId[strippedCh] ?? byStrippedId[ch.name] ?? byNormalizedName[_normalize(strippedCh)];`. Replace with a form that nulls out ambiguous branches:
    final tier4norm = _normalize(strippedCh);
    final tier4 = (ambiguousStripped.contains(strippedCh) ? null : byStrippedId[strippedCh]) ??
        (ambiguousStripped.contains(ch.name) ? null : byStrippedId[ch.name]) ??
        (ambiguousNorms.contains(tier4norm) ? null : byNormalizedName[tier4norm]);
When tier4 is null the code already falls through to fuzzy tiers, which is the desired behavior for an ambiguous key.

Do NOT record these skips as MatchTier.ambiguous here — they simply fall through to lower tiers and ultimately to `none` if nothing else matches. (Optional: only if the team wants telemetry, add a MatchTier.ambiguous record when ALL tiers fail on a key that was in an ambiguous set — but the minimal correct change is to fall through.)
- **Blast radius:** Confined to matchWithReport in this file. Effect: channels whose normalized/stripped key is genuinely ambiguous (e.g. two distinct feeds both normalizing to 'espn') now fall through to fuzzy tiers instead of silently binding to whichever XMLTV entry the Map iterated last. This can REDUCE tier3/tier4 counts and INCREASE none/fuzzy counts for ambiguous feeds — expected. No caller signature change (EpgMatcher.match / matchWithReport return types unchanged). Callers: grep for `EpgMatcher.match` / `matchWithReport` across lib (likely a refresh/epg-match service); they consume the returned Map<int,String> and are unaffected structurally.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC + TEST. Add test/backend/epg_matcher_test.dart with test name 'tier3 skips ambiguous normalized-name collisions'. Build a channelMap with two DISTINCT ids that normalize identically, e.g. {'espn.east': 'ESPN HD', 'espn.west': 'US| ESPN 4K'} and a channel named 'ESPN'. Assert: the returned map either does NOT contain the channel's id, OR (if a later fuzzy tier resolves it deterministically) the value is not silently one-of-two by Map insertion order — the key assertion is `expect(result[chId], isNot('espn.east') /* nor guaranteed 'espn.west' */)` is fragile, so instead assert the ambiguity was NOT resolved at tier 3: run matchWithReport and `expect(report.counts[MatchTier.normalizedName] ?? 0, 0)`. Also add 'tier3 still matches a unique normalized name' with a non-colliding map to prove no regression.

#### 139. [P2] epg_matcher.dart:~330 — Callsign tier matches ordinary all-caps words (KIDS, WILD, WEST) via unbounded substring against every EPG id

- **Anchor:** EpgMatcher._callsignRe / _extractCallsigns (grep `RegExp(r'\b[KW][A-Z]{3}\b')`) and the tier-6 loop in matchWithReport (grep `if (!epgId.toLowerCase().contains(csLower)) continue;`)
- **Current code:**
```dart
          for (final epgId in epgIds) {
            if (!epgId.toLowerCase().contains(csLower)) continue;
            if (epgId.length < bestEpgLen) {
```
- **Fix:** Two coordinated changes (correctness). Apply together with finding 3 (same loop).

CHANGE 1 — stoplist of common English 4-letter K/W words so obvious non-callsigns never enter the tier. Add a static set near `_callsignRe`:
    static const _callsignStopwords = <String>{
      'kids', 'wild', 'west', 'wide', 'wine', 'work', 'walk', 'wall', 'want',
      'warm', 'wash', 'wave', 'ways', 'wear', 'week', 'well', 'went', 'were',
      'what', 'when', 'whom', 'wind', 'wing', 'wins', 'wire', 'wise', 'wish',
      'with', 'wolf', 'wood', 'word', 'wore', 'worn', 'kind', 'king', 'know',
      'knew', 'keep', 'kept', 'kick', 'kill', 'knee',
    };
and filter in _extractCallsigns:
    return _callsignRe.allMatches(originalName).map((m) => m.group(0)!)
        .where((cs) => !_callsignStopwords.contains(cs.toLowerCase()))
        .toList(growable: false);

CHANGE 2 — require the callsign to appear at a WORD/SEGMENT BOUNDARY of the EPG id, not anywhere. Replace the unbounded `.contains(csLower)` guard in the tier-6 loop with a boundary check. Because EPG ids look like 'cbskxdf.us' or 'kxdf.us', treat non-alphanumeric AND case-transition (lower→UPPER in the original id) as boundaries. Simplest robust rule operating on the lowercased id + a set of segment tokens: precompute per-id the set of alnum runs split on non-alnum, e.g. for 'cbskxdf.us' -> {'cbskxdf','us'}; a callsign matches only if some segment EQUALS the callsign OR STARTS/ENDS with it. Concretely, change the guard to:
    if (!_callsignHitsBoundary(epgIdsLower[j], csLower)) continue;
where `epgIdsLower` is the precomputed lowercase list from finding 3 and `j` is the loop index (see finding 3 for making the loop indexed). Add helper:
    static bool _callsignHitsBoundary(String epgIdLower, String csLower) {
      var idx = epgIdLower.indexOf(csLower);
      while (idx != -1) {
        final before = idx == 0 ? null : epgIdLower.codeUnitAt(idx - 1);
        final afterPos = idx + csLower.length;
        final after = afterPos >= epgIdLower.length ? null : epgIdLower.codeUnitAt(afterPos);
        bool isAlnum(int? c) => c != null && ((c >= 0x30 && c <= 0x39) || (c >= 0x61 && c <= 0x7a));
        // boundary on at least one side that is not another letter/digit run midway,
        // i.e. the callsign is a prefix, suffix, or whole segment of an alnum run.
        if (!isAlnum(before) || !isAlnum(after)) return true;
        idx = epgIdLower.indexOf(csLower, idx + 1);
      }
      return false;
    }
This still catches the intended 'KXDF' -> 'cbskxdf.us' (KXDF is a suffix of the 'cbskxdf' segment, so `after` is '.') and 'kxdf.us' (prefix), while rejecting a callsign buried mid-run with alnum on both sides. Keep the shortest-id tie/skip logic unchanged.

NOTE: the header comment above _callsignRe claims '-TV/-DT/-CD suffixes handled by word boundary' — leave the regex `\b[KW][A-Z]{3}\b` as-is (still exactly-4 to avoid WGN/CNN); the stoplist + boundary check are the fix, not the regex.
- **Blast radius:** Confined to matchWithReport tier 6 + the two helpers in this file. Correctness effect: fewer wrong callsign matches (DISCOVERY KIDS, WILD EARTH, WEST TV no longer bind to unrelated ids). May slightly reduce MatchTier.callsign count and push borderline channels to tier 7/none — acceptable per 'better unmatched than wrong'. Must be applied jointly with finding 3 (same loop, shares `epgIdsLower`). No caller/signature change; no second file.
- **Acceptance:** TEST. In test/backend/epg_matcher_test.dart add 'callsign tier ignores common english K/W words'. channelMap = {'kidstv.fr':'Kids TV FR', 'kxdf.us':'CBS KXDF'}; channels = [Channel(id:1,name:'DISCOVERY KIDS HD'), Channel(id:2,name:'CBS KXDF Fairbanks')]. Assert `expect(result[1], isNot('kidstv.fr'))` (KIDS is stoplisted, no wrong bind) and `expect(result[2], 'kxdf.us')` (real callsign still matched at a boundary). Also add 'callsign requires boundary not mid-run': channelMap={'workday.com':'Workday'}, channel name 'WORK HARD' -> expect no match to 'workday.com' (WORK is stoplisted; if you drop it from the stoplist for the test, assert boundary logic instead). Run: flutter test test/backend/epg_matcher_test.dart.

#### 140. [P3] epg_matcher.dart:~207 — Tier-6 callsign matching scans the full EPG id list per channel with per-iteration toLowerCase() · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** EpgMatcher.matchWithReport tier-6 loop: grep `for (final epgId in epgIds) {` immediately followed by `if (!epgId.toLowerCase().contains(csLower)) continue;`
- **Current code:**
```dart
        for (final cs in callsigns) {
          final csLower = cs.toLowerCase();
          for (final epgId in epgIds) {
            if (!epgId.toLowerCase().contains(csLower)) continue;
            if (epgId.length < bestEpgLen) {
```
- **Fix:** Hoist the lowercasing out of the per-channel/per-callsign inner loop so `toLowerCase()` runs O(|epg|) ONCE per call instead of O(channels x callsigns x |epg|).

STEP A — precompute the lowercase id list ONCE, right after the map-building for-loop finishes populating `epgIds` (i.e. just before the `tokenIndex` build, ~line 104). Add:
    // Lowercased EPG ids, computed once, reused by tier 6 (callsign substring).
    final epgIdsLower = <String>[for (final id in epgIds) id.toLowerCase()];

STEP B — rewrite the tier-6 inner loop to index into both parallel lists and drop the per-iteration allocation. Replace:
        for (final cs in callsigns) {
          final csLower = cs.toLowerCase();
          for (final epgId in epgIds) {
            if (!epgId.toLowerCase().contains(csLower)) continue;
            if (epgId.length < bestEpgLen) {
              bestEpgLen = epgId.length;
              bestId = epgId;
              bestCount = 1;
            } else if (epgId.length == bestEpgLen && epgId != bestId) {
              bestCount++;
            }
          }
        }
with:
        for (final cs in callsigns) {
          final csLower = cs.toLowerCase();
          for (var j = 0; j < epgIds.length; j++) {
            final epgIdLower = epgIdsLower[j];
            if (!_callsignHitsBoundary(epgIdLower, csLower)) continue; // finding 2 boundary check
            final epgId = epgIds[j];
            if (epgId.length < bestEpgLen) {
              bestEpgLen = epgId.length;
              bestId = epgId;
              bestCount = 1;
            } else if (epgId.length == bestEpgLen && epgId != bestId) {
              bestCount++;
            }
          }
        }
(If finding 2 is not yet applied, temporarily use `if (!epgIdLower.contains(csLower)) continue;` — but apply finding 2 in the same edit; both target this loop.)

This keeps behavior identical to the pre-fix scan (same candidate set, same shortest-id tie rule) while eliminating ~|channels|x|callsigns| redundant lowercasings. A stronger 4-gram/callsign inverted index is possible but NOT required for this fix — the one-time lowercasing hoist is the smallest correct change and removes the per-iteration allocation the finding calls out.
- **Blast radius:** Confined to matchWithReport in this file. Same result set as before (boundary change is finding 2's concern, not this one). Shares `epgIdsLower` with finding 2 — declare it once. No caller/signature change; no second file. Perf-only for the substring-scan cost; the O(channels x |epg|) fan-out itself is unchanged (still a full scan per callsign-bearing channel) — this fix removes the allocation constant, not the asymptotic factor. If profiling later shows the linear scan still dominates, escalate to a callsign->id index as a follow-up.
- **Acceptance:** MANUAL/DEVICE for the perf win: cannot be proven from source alone — it requires a US-heavy large source (150k+ channels x 100k+ XMLTV ids). On an onn 4K Plus (2GB) run a forced Re-match against such a source and confirm the tier-6 phase no longer allocates per-id (observable as reduced GC pressure / lower wall time in the match isolate log). PLUS a cheap STATIC/TEST guard against regression: add test 'tier6 result unchanged after lowercase hoist' asserting a real callsign match (channelMap={'cbskxdf.us':'CBS KXDF'}, channel 'CBS KXDF Fairbanks' -> expect result == 'cbskxdf.us'), proving the indexed loop preserves matching. Correctness is testable; the perf delta is device/scale-only.

#### 141. [P2] utils.dart:~216 — Background WorkManager EPG isolate writes the channels DB while the main-isolate refresh holds minutes-long wr · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** Utils.refreshAllSources → the top-level `await Sql.withSuspendedFtsTriggers(() async {` wrapper (grep `withSuspendedFtsTriggers` in utils.dart); the matching `batchTargetedRebuild: () async {});` closes it. The background side is epg_service.dart `callbackDispatcher` → `EpgService.refreshAllSources(background: true)` → `Sql.setChannelEpgIds(merged)` (grep `setChannelEpgIds` in epg_service.dart).
- **Current code:**
```dart
    await Sql.withSuspendedFtsTriggers(() async {
      await Sql.withDroppedBrowseIndexes(() async {
        // fix611: one source failing must NEVER stop the rest from
```
- **Fix:** Add a cross-isolate advisory lock backed by the existing MAIN-db `app_meta` table and have BOTH the foreground catalog refresh and the background EPG matcher respect it.

DECISION: use a cooperative skip (background yields to foreground), NOT a blocking wait — a 2 GB TV box must never have two isolates fighting for the single sqlite writer, and the background EPG match is deferrable (it re-runs on the next WorkManager cadence). Foreground (user-initiated) always wins.

STEP 1 — add helpers to lib/backend/sql.dart (near checkpointAndTruncateWal). The lock row lives in db.sqlite `app_meta` (already exists, key TEXT PRIMARY KEY / value TEXT — db_factory.dart migration 39). Store an owner tag + a wall-clock expiry so a crashed holder cannot deadlock forever:

  static const String _refreshLockKey = 'refresh_lock';
  /// Best-effort cross-isolate advisory lock in db.sqlite app_meta.
  /// Returns true if acquired. `owner` is a free label ('foreground'/'background').
  /// `staleAfter` lets a crashed holder's stale lock be reclaimed.
  static Future<bool> tryAcquireRefreshLock(String owner,
      {Duration staleAfter = const Duration(minutes: 45)}) async {
    final db = await DbFactory.db;
    final now = DateTime.now().millisecondsSinceEpoch;
    return await db.writeTransaction((tx) async {
      final row = await tx.getOptional(
          "SELECT value FROM app_meta WHERE key = ?", [_refreshLockKey]);
      if (row != null && (row['value'] as String?) != null) {
        final parts = (row['value'] as String).split('|'); // owner|acquiredMs
        final acquiredMs = int.tryParse(parts.length > 1 ? parts[1] : '') ?? 0;
        if (now - acquiredMs < staleAfter.inMilliseconds) return false; // held & fresh
      }
      await tx.execute(
          "INSERT OR REPLACE INTO app_meta (key, value) VALUES (?, ?)",
          [_refreshLockKey, '$owner|$now']);
      return true;
    });
  }
  static Future<void> releaseRefreshLock() async {
    final db = await DbFactory.db;
    await db.execute("DELETE FROM app_meta WHERE key = ?", [_refreshLockKey]);
  }

STEP 2 — in utils.dart Utils.refreshAllSources, wrap the whole withSuspendedFtsTriggers block AND the trailing checkpointAndTruncateWal in a lock. Change the first snippet region so it becomes:

    final gotLock = await Sql.tryAcquireRefreshLock('foreground');
    // Foreground refresh always proceeds even if the lock read failed; the lock
    // is advisory and the background side is the one that must yield.
    try {
      await Sql.withSuspendedFtsTriggers(() async {
        ... (existing body unchanged) ...
      }, batchTargetedRebuild: () async {});
      try {
        await Sql.checkpointAndTruncateWal(epg: false);
      } catch (e) { ...existing warn... }
    } finally {
      if (gotLock) await Sql.releaseRefreshLock();
    }

STEP 3 — in epg_service.dart, guard ONLY the background path. In `refreshAllSources({bool background = false})`, at the very top add:

    if (background) {
      final ok = await Sql.tryAcquireRefreshLock('background');
      if (!ok) {
        AppLog.info('EPG: skipping background refresh — a catalog refresh holds the lock');
        return;
      }
    }
    try { ...existing loop... }
    finally { if (background) await Sql.releaseRefreshLock(); }

Do NOT gate the foreground EpgService.refreshAllSources(background:false) path — that is user-initiated and may legitimately overlap nothing. This makes the foreground catalog refresh and the background EPG matcher mutually exclusive across isolates, closing the SQLITE_BUSY window on setChannelEpgIds and the check-then-use race on the gated `INDEXED BY idx_epg_unmatched` (sql.dart getChannelsNeedingEpgMatch line ~3103) because the background matcher no longer runs while the foreground drop is in flight.
- **Blast radius:** Touches THREE files: utils.dart (wrap block), sql.dart (2 new helpers, reuses existing app_meta table — no migration), epg_service.dart (background guard in refreshAllSources). The lock is advisory/best-effort: if app_meta write fails, foreground still proceeds (fail-open for the user action) and background skips (fail-safe). A crashed foreground holder is reclaimed after staleAfter (45 min > worst-case single refresh). Does NOT change the single-source Utils.processSource path — that path also writes channels but is user-initiated and short-lived; if you want full safety, also wrap Utils.refreshSource similarly, but that is out of scope for this finding (note it). Verify no OTHER background writer to db.sqlite exists that should also honor the lock (grep for other Workmanager().executeTask entry points).
- **Acceptance:** STATIC: add a unit test `refresh_lock_test.dart` asserting `Sql.tryAcquireRefreshLock('a')` returns true then a second `tryAcquireRefreshLock('b')` returns false until `releaseRefreshLock()`, and that a lock older than staleAfter is reclaimable (seed app_meta with an old timestamp). CANNOT be fully proven without a device: the actual cross-isolate SQLITE_BUSY race requires a WorkManager isolate + a >1M-row source on 2 GB hardware — MANUAL/DEVICE: on an Android TV box (onn 4K/Shield), trigger a full catalog refresh, force the epg_refresh WorkManager task concurrently (adb `cmd jobscheduler run -f <pkg> <jobid>` or wait for cadence), and confirm the log shows 'EPG: skipping background refresh — a catalog refresh holds the lock' and NO 'database is locked'/'code 5' in either isolate's log.

#### 142. [P3] utils.dart:~88 — Browse indexes are dropped before the network fetch even starts, extending the no-index window (degraded brows · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** Utils.processSource → the `await Sql.withDroppedBrowseIndexes(() async {` that wraps the whole `switch (source.sourceType)` fetch dispatch (grep `dispatching ${source.sourceType} fetch` in utils.dart). The write phase proper is xtream.dart getXtream's `await Sql.commitWriteBatched(` (grep `committing ${statements.length} statement-closures`).

```dart

        AppLog.info('fix617 processSource: "${source.name}" — indexes dropped,'
            ' dispatching ${source.sourceType} fetch');
        switch (source.sourceType) {
```
- **Fix:** DECISION: choose the SMALLER, lower-risk variant of the proposed fix — move the index drop OUT of Utils.processSource and DOWN into each fetcher so it wraps only the DB-write phase, not the network fetch. Do NOT attempt to pre-build the statements list in processSource (that would require returning the closure list up through three fetchers and is a large refactor with its own blast radius).

Concretely: in Utils.processSource, REMOVE the `withDroppedBrowseIndexes` wrapper around the switch — call the fetchers directly:

        switch (source.sourceType) {
          case SourceType.m3u:
            await processM3U(source, wipe, null, onProgress);
            break;
          case SourceType.m3uUrl:

Then in xtream.dart getXtream, wrap ONLY the commit — change the existing `await Sql.withSuspendedFtsTriggers(() async { await Sql.commitWriteBatched(...) }, refreshedSourceId: source.id);` to also be inside `await Sql.withDroppedBrowseIndexes(() async { <that withSuspendedFtsTriggers block> }, onProgress: onProgress);`. Do the same in m3u.dart processM3U around its `await Sql.commitWriteBatched(batch, memory: memory);` (m3u.dart:70) and in processM3UUrl's write. `withDroppedBrowseIndexes` is already re-entrant (sql.dart line 487, `_browseIndexesDropped` early-return), so the outer whole-loop drop in refreshAllSources still owns drop+recreate and the per-fetcher wrap becomes a pass-through during a batch — only the single-source processSource path narrows.

EFFECT: on the single-source path, the ~19 browse indexes now stay live through the entire download phase and drop only for the seconds-to-minutes commit, shrinking the degraded-browse window from (download+commit) to (commit).
- **Blast radius:** Touches THREE files: utils.dart (remove wrapper), xtream.dart (add wrapper around commit block only), m3u.dart (add wrapper around processM3U commit + processM3UUrl commit). CRITICAL ORDERING: in refreshAllSources the outer whole-loop `withDroppedBrowseIndexes` sets `_browseIndexesDropped=true` so the new per-fetcher wrap is a no-op there — verify the re-entrancy guard truly early-returns before touching the DB (sql.dart line 487-491, confirmed). The single-source path currently relies on withDroppedBrowseIndexes being the OUTER wrapper for the fix521/fix518 FTS-suspend ordering note (sql.dart comment line 535-537 'on the single-source path withDroppedBrowseIndexes is the OUTER wrapper'); after this change getXtream nests withDroppedBrowseIndexes OUTSIDE withSuspendedFtsTriggers to preserve that ordering — verify the FTS rebuild still fires exactly once on the single-source path. Do NOT change refreshAllSources.

Add a widget/integration-free unit assertion is hard here; MANUAL/DEVICE (onn 4K): with a fresh single Xtream source refresh in progress, open Browse during the DOWNLOAD phase and confirm it responds in the fast (indexed, single-digit ms) range rather than the 10-45 s unindexed-scan range; then confirm during the COMMIT phase it degrades. Cannot be proven without a device + a large (>100k-row) source because the perf delta only manifests at scale.

#### 143. [P3] utils.dart:~230 — Cancel during refresh-all has no effect mid-source: a large source (including the unbounded per-category VOD r

- **Anchor:** Utils.refreshAllSources → the ONLY `shouldCancel?.call()` check, guarded by 'cancelled by user before source' (grep `cancelled by user before` in utils.dart). Downstream sinks: xtream.dart getXtream, xtream.dart `_fetchVodPerCategory` (grep `for (final cat in vodCats)`), sql.dart commitWriteBatched (grep `for (var i = 0; i < commits.length; i += batchSize)`).
- **Current code:**
```dart
          if (shouldCancel?.call() ?? false) {
            AppLog.info('Utils.refreshAllSources: cancelled by user before '
                'source ${i + 1}/${enabled.length}');
            break;
          }
```
- **Fix:** Thread the existing `shouldCancel` predicate down into the fetch and commit layers so cancellation takes effect MID-source, not only between sources. DECISION: use a cooperative check (no exception-throwing token) that aborts at the two coarsest safe boundaries — per HTTP request and per commit batch — matching the existing between-source pattern.

STEP 1 — widen the plumbing signatures to carry `bool Function()? shouldCancel`:
  - Utils.refreshSource(Source source, {onProgress, onRowProgress, bool Function()? shouldCancel}) — add param, pass through to processSource.
  - Utils.processSource(source, [wipe, onProgress, onRowProgress, bool Function()? shouldCancel]) — add param, pass into the sourceType switch calls.
  - In refreshAllSources, at the `await refreshSource(s, ...)` call inside the retry loop, pass `shouldCancel: shouldCancel`.
  - xtream.dart getXtream(source, wipe, [onProgress, onRowProgress, bool Function()? shouldCancel]).
  - xtream.dart _fetchVodPerCategory(source, vodCats, bulk, onProgress, {bool Function()? shouldCancel}).
  - sql.dart commitWriteBatched(commits, {batchSize, memory, onBatchCommitted, bool Function()? shouldCancel}).

STEP 2 — enforce it at the loop bodies:
  - _fetchVodPerCategory: at the top of `for (final cat in vodCats)` add `if (shouldCancel?.call() ?? false) break;` (return what has been collected so far — the caller treats a short result the same as a truncated fetch, which is acceptable on cancel).
  - getXtream: BEFORE the `commitWriteBatched` write phase add `if (shouldCancel?.call() ?? false) { onProgress?.call('Cancelled'); return; }` so a cancel during download skips the write entirely for the in-flight source.
  - commitWriteBatched: at the top of the `for (var i = 0; ...)` batch loop add `if (shouldCancel?.call() ?? false) { AppLog.info('Sql.commitWriteBatched: cancelled after $batchIndex batch(es)'); break; }`. Aborting BETWEEN transactions is safe — each commitWrite is its own transaction; a partial-source write is recoverable because the NEXT refresh wipes+reinserts that source.

Do NOT add cancel checks INSIDE a single commitWrite transaction (would leave a half-written batch mid-transaction). Do NOT throw on cancel — the existing refreshAllSources retry loop would treat a thrown cancel as a failure and retry it; a clean early-return/break is required.
- **Blast radius:** Touches THREE files (utils.dart, xtream.dart, sql.dart). CAUTION: getXtream commits the source row UP FRONT (xtream.dart:44 commitWrite getOrCreateSourceByName) BEFORE the cancellable fetch — a cancel after that point leaves the source row present but its channels un-wiped/partial; that is the SAME state a between-source cancel already produces (fix620 comment 'Sources already refreshed keep their data') so it is acceptable, but confirm the source is not left `enabled=false` or count-zeroed by a partial run. commitWriteBatched has OTHER callers (grep `commitWriteBatched(` across lib/) — m3u.dart:70 and any others — the new param is optional so existing calls compile unchanged; only refresh callers need to pass it. Verify onRowProgress semantics still make sense after an early break (progress will stop mid-way, which is correct for a cancel).
- **Acceptance:** Add unit test `commit_write_batched_cancel_test.dart`: build a `commits` list of e.g. 10 no-op closures with batchSize=2, pass `shouldCancel: () => callCount >= 2` (increment a counter each closure), and assert FEWER than all 10 closures ran (i.e. the batch loop broke early). For _fetchVodPerCategory add `fetch_vod_cancel_test.dart` asserting that with `shouldCancel: () => true` it returns immediately with only the `bulk` seed entries and issues zero per-category HTTP calls (inject a fake fetcher counting calls). MANUAL/DEVICE (onn 4K, >100k-row source): start refresh-all, hit Cancel mid-download of source 1, and confirm from the log that no further `getXtreamHttpData` category calls fire and `commitWriteBatched` logs 'cancelled after N batch(es)' rather than 'DONE' — cannot be timed meaningfully without a large source on-device.

#### 147. [P2] overlay_player_controller.dart:~198 — OverlayPlayerController.startOverlay has no reentrancy guard — interleaved start/stop leaks a live engine or l · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** OverlayPlayerController.startOverlay — grep for `Future<void> startOverlay(` and the local `final engine = MpvEngine(`; guard field added near `MpvEngine? _engine;` (grep `MpvEngine? _engine;`)
- **Current code:**
```dart
    await _disposeEngine();
    _channel = ch;
    _settings = s;
    _source = src;
    notifyListeners();

    final url = ch.url;
    if (url == null || url.isEmpty) return;
```
- **Fix:** Add a generation token so a superseded in-flight startOverlay disposes its locally-created engine instead of leaking it, and so a stopOverlay racing an in-flight start wins.

Step 1 — declare the field with the other private fields (right after `MpvEngine? _engine;` near L27):
  `int _startGeneration = 0;`

Step 2 — at the very top of startOverlay body (as the first statements, before `await _disposeEngine();`) capture and bump the token:
  `final int gen = ++_startGeneration;`

Step 3 — after `await _disposeEngine();` and before mutating `_channel/_settings/_source`, bail if superseded:
  `if (gen != _startGeneration) return;`
  (Place this immediately after the `await _disposeEngine();` line, above `_channel = ch;`.)

Step 4 — after `await engine.setVolume(fullScreenActive ? 0.0 : 1.0);` and BEFORE `_engine = engine;`, re-check; if superseded, dispose the local engine and return so it is not stored and does not keep decoding:
  `if (gen != _startGeneration) { await engine.dispose(); return; }`

Step 5 — after the final `await engine.open(url: url);` succeeds, guard the success path: if superseded during open, the newer call already ran `_disposeEngine()` which would NOT have caught this engine (it was stored at Step past). To be safe, after `_engine = engine;` (Step 4) the engine is owned by the controller, so a later start's `_disposeEngine()` correctly disposes it — no extra step needed there. Just ensure Step 4's re-check is present.

Step 6 — in stopOverlay, bump the generation so any in-flight startOverlay is invalidated. Add as the first statement of stopOverlay (before `await _disposeEngine();`):
  `++_startGeneration;`

Do NOT add a mutex/lock; the monotonic int is sufficient and matches the per-isolate singleton model.
- **Blast radius:** Only OverlayPlayerController methods that create/dispose the overlay engine: startOverlay and stopOverlay (this file). detachOverlayEngine/adoptOverlayEngine mutate _engine directly but do not create engines via startOverlay, so they are unaffected; however if a future concern arises, adoptOverlayEngine could also `++_startGeneration` — NOT required for this fix. Callers of startOverlay (mini-player 'Watch in mini-player' button, swap path with forceMuted) get the intended behavior: a double-invocation no longer leaks the first engine. No second file needs editing. The added `await engine.dispose()` in Step 4 relies on MpvEngine.dispose being idempotent/safe on a never-opened engine — MpvEngine is constructed but open() has not run at Step 4, so dispose must tolerate a pre-open engine (verify).
- **Acceptance:** verify_first premise (that dispose is safe pre-open) must be confirmed, then: add unit test `startOverlay_superseded_disposes_orphan_engine` — inject a fake MpvEngine factory (or use a subclass hook) so the test can await two overlapping startOverlay calls with different channels; assert (a) OverlayPlayerController.instance.engine corresponds to the SECOND channel, and (b) the first channel's engine received a dispose() call and never had open() left running. ### `lib/backend/epg_discovery/variants/stalker_xmltv_query_auth.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P2×1]

**File notes:** Only ONE finding in this file, so no ordering concern. The edit is entirely inside StalkerXmltvQueryAuth.probe. Key constraints for the implementer: (1) dart:async (Completer/StreamSubscription) and package:http (Request/Response/Client) are ALREADY imported — no new imports. (2) Do NOT modify epg_validator.dart or the isValidEpgResponse signature; construct a synthetic http.Response.bytes(capped, streamed.statusCode, headers: streamed.headers) so the validator's status/content-type checks still work against the 64KB head. (3) The success EpgDiscoveryResult return must move inside the new inner try so `client.close()` in a finally always runs; the existing `on TimeoutException`/`catch (e)` outer handlers stay and still return null. (4) Cancel the subscription as soon as bodyBytes.length >= EpgValidator.headBytesCap so the socket read stops — this is the whole point of the fix. (5) Sibling variants (stalker_xmltv_cookie_auth.dart, xtream_m3u_tvg_url.dart) share the pattern but are OUT OF SCOPE here.

#### 149. [P2] stalker_xmltv_query_auth.dart:~35 — Variant 1 buffers the entire XMLTV feed to validate only the first 64KB · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** class StalkerXmltvQueryAuth, static Future probe(...) — grep for the block `final resp = await http` + `final bodyBytes = resp.bodyBytes;` (this is the ONLY http.get in the file)
- **Current code:**
```dart
      final resp = await http
          .get(url, headers: const {'User-Agent': 'Free4Me-IPTV/1.0'})
          .timeout(_timeout);
      final bodyBytes = resp.bodyBytes;
      if (!EpgValidator.isValidEpgResponse(resp, bodyBytes)) {
```
- **Fix:** Replace the buffered `http.get` with a streamed read that stops after headBytesCap bytes, then feed a synthetic http.Response (status+headers from the streamed response, body = capped head bytes) to the UNCHANGED validator. Concrete edit — replace the snippet's 5 lines with:

```
      final request = http.Request('GET', url)
        ..headers['User-Agent'] = 'Free4Me-IPTV/1.0';
      final client = http.Client();
      final List<int> bodyBytes = [];
      try {
        final streamed = await client.send(request).timeout(_timeout);
        // Read only enough to validate; cancel once we have the cap.
        final completer = Completer<void>();
        late final StreamSubscription<List<int>> sub;
        sub = streamed.stream.timeout(_timeout).listen(
          (chunk) {
            bodyBytes.addAll(chunk);
            if (bodyBytes.length >= EpgValidator.headBytesCap) {
              sub.cancel();
              if (!completer.isCompleted) completer.complete();
            }
          },
          onDone: () {
            if (!completer.isCompleted) completer.complete();
          },
          onError: (Object e) {
            if (!completer.isCompleted) completer.completeError(e);
          },
          cancelOnError: true,
        );
        await completer.future;
        final capped = bodyBytes.length > EpgValidator.headBytesCap
            ? bodyBytes.sublist(0, EpgValidator.headBytesCap)
            : bodyBytes;
        final resp = http.Response.bytes(
          capped,
          streamed.statusCode,
          headers: streamed.headers,
        );
        if (!EpgValidator.isValidEpgResponse(resp, capped)) {
```

Then the existing `AppLog.info('...rejected by validator'); return null; }` and the success `EpgDiscoveryResult` block that follow stay as-is, but the success block and its `return` must move INSIDE this inner `try`. Close that inner try with a `finally { client.close(); }` before the existing `on TimeoutException`/`catch (e)` handlers (which remain unchanged and still return null). Note: the gzip branch means only the first 64KB of a gzip stream is captured — that is fine because EpgValidator.isXmltvGzip only checks the first 2 magic bytes and returns true. `dart:async` is already imported (line 1); `package:http/http.dart as http` already imported (line 3). No validator/import changes needed. Keep `final start`/elapsed logic exactly as-is.
- **Blast radius:** Single-file change. EpgValidator signature and epg_validator.dart are UNCHANGED — it still receives an http.Response (built via http.Response.bytes) + capped body, and only reads statusCode + headers['content-type'] + the byte list, all of which the synthetic response provides. Does NOT touch the sibling variants stalker_xmltv_cookie_auth.dart (line 114) or xtream_m3u_tvg_url.dart (lines 71-94) — those have the same buffering issue but are out of scope for THIS finding; do not edit them here. Behavioral parity risk: previously `resp.bodyBytes` returned the FULL body and the validator's 8KB/64KB windows saw the whole doc; now they see at most 64KB, which is >= both internal windows (8192 and 65536-driven greps), so validation verdicts are identical for any real feed. New client.close() ensures no socket leak per probe.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC (fast, deterministic): add test `variant1 stops reading after headBytesCap bytes` in a new/existing test under test/ using a MockClient (package:http/testing.dart) whose send() returns a http.StreamedResponse backed by a Stream that yields a valid XMLTV head chunk (contains `<?xml`, `<tv`, one `<programme `) followed by a chunk that increments a counter each time it is pulled; assert (a) probe(...) returns a non-null EpgDiscoveryResult with variant=='stalker-xmltv-query', and (b) the source stream was canceled — i.e. the post-64KB counter stays 0 / the generator does not run to completion. Because http.get vs client.send differ, the test MUST inject the client; if probe() cannot currently take an injected http.Client, the smallest acceptable change is to add an optional named `http.Client? client` param to probe() defaulting to `http.Client()` (document this in the fix if the reviewer wants the test) OR mark the acceptance as MANUAL/DEVICE. MANUAL/DEVICE fallback (no injectable client): on an Android TV box, add a temporary large real Xtream source and confirm via `adb logcat` that variant1 logs 'hit'/'rejected' within the 5s timeout and app RSS does not spike by the feed size (tens–hundreds of MB) during discovery — this proves the memory win but is not CI-provable.
- **Notes:** verify_first=true: the memory-blowup premise depends on the provider actually streaming a multi-MB body on a 200 to xmltv.php (many portals gzip or 404 fast). Confirm with one real large source that the OLD code buffers the whole feed before changing behavior; the fix is safe regardless, but the P2 severity hinges on that runtime observation.

### `lib/backend/http_client.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P2×1]

**File notes:** Only ONE finding targets this file, so ordering within http_client.dart is trivial. The chosen fix is additive: it adds a new enum + an optional out-parameter to getWithRetry and leaves the existing `http.Response?` return type and all early-null control flow byte-for-byte intact. That means the two passive callers (lib/backend/update_checker.dart:126 and lib/backend/xtream_epg.dart:85) compile and behave unchanged with no edits.

Cross-file work required to make the finding's user-visible benefit real lives in lib/backend/xtream.dart, NOT this file. Apply in this order:
1. First edit lib/backend/http_client.dart (add the `HttpFailureKind` enum at top-of-file below imports, add the optional `void Function(HttpFailureKind)? onFailure` param to getWithRetry, and invoke it at each non-200 / exception exit).
2. Then edit lib/backend/xtream.dart:getXtreamHttpData (line ~364) to pass an onFailure callback, capture the kind, and propagate a permanent-auth signal upward (simplest concrete propagation: set `source.status = 'disabled'` when kind == HttpFailureKind.authRejected, which is already honored by isSourceExpired() at xtream.dart:449, and log a distinct warn). This reuses the EXISTING Source.status field (lib/models/source.dart:53) — no new model field or DB column needed.

Shared helper/import: no new package import is needed (dart:io is already imported for SocketException/HttpException). The new `HttpFailureKind` enum is the only new symbol; export nothing special — it lives in http_client.dart and is imported wherever http_client.dart already is.

#### 150. [P2] http_client.dart:~38 — getWithRetry collapses 4xx auth/permanent failures and transient network/timeout failures into the same null r · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** class AppHttp, method getWithRetry — grep for the loop guard `for (int attempt = 0; attempt < 2; attempt++)` and the `if (resp.statusCode != 200) return null;` line inside it
- **Current code:**
```dart
        if (resp.statusCode >= 500 && resp.statusCode < 600 && attempt == 0) {
          await Future.delayed(const Duration(milliseconds: 500));
          continue;
        }
        if (resp.statusCode != 200) return null;
        return resp;
```
- **Fix:** Add a caller-inspectable failure class instead of refactoring the return type (keeps the two passive callers untouched). Steps, all within lib/backend/http_client.dart:

(1) Add this enum immediately after the imports (below `import 'package:http/io_client.dart';`, above `class AppHttp {`):

    /// Classifies why an AppHttp request did not yield a 200 body, so callers
    /// can distinguish PERMANENT failures (auth/credentials/gone — do not keep
    /// retrying forever) from TRANSIENT ones (timeout/socket/5xx — safe to
    /// preserve prior data and try again later).
    enum HttpFailureKind {
      /// 401/403 (and 407): credentials rejected. Permanent until fixed.
      authRejected,
      /// 404/410: resource/line gone. Permanent.
      notFound,
      /// Any other non-200 (incl. 5xx that survived the one retry). Transient-ish.
      httpError,
      /// TimeoutException after final attempt.
      timeout,
      /// SocketException / HttpException / other network error after final attempt.
      network,
    }

(2) Add an optional out-parameter to getWithRetry. Change its signature
    named-params block from:
        Duration timeout = const Duration(seconds: 20),
        Map<String, String>? headers,
      }) async {
    to:
        Duration timeout = const Duration(seconds: 20),
        Map<String, String>? headers,
        void Function(HttpFailureKind kind, int? statusCode)? onFailure,
      }) async {

(3) Replace the non-200 return with a classified callback. Change the snippet:
        if (resp.statusCode != 200) return null;
        return resp;
    to:
        if (resp.statusCode != 200) {
          final sc = resp.statusCode;
          if (sc == 401 || sc == 403 || sc == 407) {
            onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.authRejected, sc);
          } else if (sc == 404 || sc == 410) {
            onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.notFound, sc);
          } else {
            onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.httpError, sc);
          }
          return null;
        }
        return resp;

(4) Report the transient classes at the exception exits too (still returning null, control flow otherwise identical):
    - In `on TimeoutException catch (_) { if (attempt == 1) return null; }` change the body to:
        if (attempt == 1) { onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.timeout, null); return null; }
    - In `on SocketException catch (_) { if (attempt == 1) return null; ... }` change the first line to:
        if (attempt == 1) { onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.network, null); return null; }
    - In `on HttpException catch (_) { return null; }` change to:
        onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.network, null); return null;
    - In the trailing `catch (_) { return null; }` change to:
        onFailure?.call(HttpFailureKind.network, null); return null;

Leave the return type `Future<http.Response?>` and every `return null;`/`continue;` exactly as-is otherwise. Do NOT throw — throwing would break update_checker.dart and xtream_epg.dart which only null-check.

SECOND FILE (required to realize the finding's benefit) — lib/backend/xtream.dart, function getXtreamHttpData (~line 364, the `final response = await AppHttp.getWithRetry(` call): pass an onFailure callback that records the kind, and act on a permanent auth reject. Concretely, before the getWithRetry call declare `HttpFailureKind? failKind;`, pass `onFailure: (k, sc) => failKind = k,` into the call, and after `if (response == null) return null;` insert:
        if (failKind == HttpFailureKind.authRejected) {
          AppLog.warn('Xtream: credentials REJECTED (auth) action="$action" '
              'source="${source.name}" — flagging source disabled');
          source.status = 'disabled';
        }
    Reusing the existing Source.status field means isSourceExpired() (xtream.dart:449) already returns true for it, so the guide/UI surfaces the dead line without any new plumbing. Add the http_client import to xtream.dart only if HttpFailureKind is not already visible (it imports http_client already for AppHttp — verify with grep `import.*http_client` in xtream.dart; if present, no new import).
- **Blast radius:** getWithRetry has 3 callers: update_checker.dart:126 and xtream_epg.dart:85 pass no onFailure and are unaffected (optional param, unchanged return semantics). xtream.dart:364 (getXtreamHttpData) is the intended consumer and is the second file that MUST be edited. Setting source.status='disabled' feeds isSourceExpired() (xtream.dart:449) — confirm no code path treats 'disabled' as a value it will overwrite on the same refresh: fetchXtreamAccountInfo (xtream.dart:420) can later set source.status from user_info — ensure the auth-reject flagging is not clobbered within the same run (auth reject means the info call also 401s, so status stays 'disabled'; still, VERIFY the ordering in refreshXtream so a later successful-looking write of status=null does not erase the flag). Whether source.status is persisted to the DB and reloaded is a separate concern in xtream.dart/Sql — confirm persistence exists before relying on the flag surviving a restart.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC + UNIT: Add a unit test `getWithRetry_classifies_permanent_vs_transient` in the http_client test file. Using a mock http.Client returning a 403, assert getWithRetry returns null AND the onFailure callback was invoked with (HttpFailureKind.authRejected, 403). A second case returning 500 twice asserts onFailure fires with HttpFailureKind.httpError (or timeout/network for exception simulation) and NOT authRejected. Assertion form: `expect(capturedKind, HttpFailureKind.authRejected);` and `expect(result, isNull);`. For the xtream.dart side: unit test that getXtreamHttpData sets source.status='disabled' when the underlying getWithRetry reports authRejected — assert `expect(source.status, 'disabled');`. The end-to-end 'expired line surfaces in the guide' behavior is DEVICE-observable only (MANUAL/DEVICE: on an Android TV box, point a source at credentials returning 403 and confirm the source shows expired/disabled rather than silently preserving a stale catalog); the unit tests above are the enforceable done-gate.

### `lib/backend/update_checker.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P2×1]

**File notes:** Single finding, but it spans several edits within update_checker.dart plus two other files. SAFE ORDER inside update_checker.dart (apply bottom-of-file upward so earlier line offsets don't shift later anchors, and because the edits are logically dependent): (1) FIRST edit `_showUpdateDialog` (near end of file, grep `await _downloadAndInstall`) to read `apkSha256` and pass it — this is the deepest anchor. (2) THEN edit `_downloadAndInstall`: add the SHA gate before `OpenFilex.open`, add `hashInput.add(chunk)` / digest setup inside the loop, change the signature. (3) THEN the scheme guard at the top of `_downloadAndInstall`. (4) THEN add `import 'package:crypto/crypto.dart';` at the top import block. Doing the signature change and its sole call site together avoids a transient compile break. SEPARATELY: add `crypto: ^3.0.0` to pubspec.yaml dependencies and run `flutter pub get`; and update the release pipeline that writes version.json to emit `apkSha256`. The scheme guard is independent and self-contained — if the team wants to ship the cheap security win first, it can land alone without the crypto dependency or version.json change. Shared helpers to introduce for testability: `_isTrustedApkScheme(Uri)` and `_shaMatches(String, String?)`, referenced by the guard/gate and by the unit test.

#### 151. [P2] update_checker.dart:~213 — In-app APK update: enforce https scheme on apkUrl and verify SHA-256 of the downloaded APK before invoking the

- **Anchor:** UpdateChecker._downloadAndInstall — grep the guard `if (uri == null) {` immediately after `final uri = Uri.tryParse(apkUrl);`, and the install handoff `final result = await OpenFilex.open(outFile.path);`. The signature is `static Future<void> _downloadAndInstall(BuildContext context, String apkUrl, String version)`.
- **Current code:**
```dart
    final uri = Uri.tryParse(apkUrl);
    if (uri == null) {
      AppLog.warn('UpdateChecker: invalid apkUrl');
      return;
    }
```
- **Fix:** Make three coordinated edits inside `_downloadAndInstall`, plus one call-site change and one pubspec change.

(1) SCHEME GUARD (smallest high-value change — apply even if the hash design is deferred). Replace the snippet above with a guard that also rejects any non-https scheme:
```
    final uri = Uri.tryParse(apkUrl);
    if (uri == null || uri.scheme.toLowerCase() != 'https') {
      AppLog.warn('UpdateChecker: apkUrl missing or not https — $apkUrl');
      if (context.mounted) {
        ScaffoldMessenger.of(context).showSnackBar(
          const SnackBar(content: Text('Update rejected: download URL is not secure (https required)')),
        );
      }
      return;
    }
```
This closes the cleartext-http vector directly (AndroidManifest sets `usesCleartextTraffic="true"`, so without this guard an http:// apkUrl is honored).

(2) SHA-256 VERIFICATION. Thread an `expectedSha256` string through the method: change the signature to `static Future<void> _downloadAndInstall(BuildContext context, String apkUrl, String version, String? expectedSha256)`. At top of file add `import 'package:crypto/crypto.dart';`. Inside the download loop, compute the digest incrementally so the >100 MB APK is never buffered in memory: before the `await for` loop add `final digestSink = AccumulatorSink<Digest>(); final hashInput = sha256.startChunkedConversion(digestSink);`. Inside the loop, right after `sink.add(chunk);`, add `hashInput.add(chunk);`. After `await sink.close();` add `hashInput.close(); final actualSha = digestSink.events.single.toString();`. Then, BEFORE the `OpenFilex.open` handoff, insert a verification gate:
```
    if (expectedSha256 != null && expectedSha256.isNotEmpty) {
      if (actualSha.toLowerCase() != expectedSha256.toLowerCase()) {
        AppLog.warn('UpdateChecker: SHA-256 mismatch expected=$expectedSha256 actual=$actualSha');
        await outFile.delete().catchError((_) => outFile!);
        if (context.mounted) {
          ScaffoldMessenger.of(context).showSnackBar(
            const SnackBar(content: Text('Update rejected: file integrity check failed')),
          );
        }
        return;
      }
      AppLog.info('UpdateChecker: SHA-256 verified');
    } else {
      AppLog.warn('UpdateChecker: no expected SHA-256 in version.json — installing unverified APK');
    }
```
DECISION: verification is enforced-if-present, warn-if-absent. Do NOT hard-block when `expectedSha256` is null, because the currently-published version.json (verified: `latest`, `releaseUrl`, `minSupportedAndroidApi`, `criticalUpdate`, `releaseNotes`, `apkUrl` — no sha field) would otherwise make every existing client unable to update. Once version.json is updated to carry the field for all future releases, a follow-up can flip this to hard-block.

(3) CALL SITE in `_showUpdateDialog` (grep `await _downloadAndInstall(context, apkUrl, remoteVersion);`). Read the sha from the version manifest and pass it: change to `final apkSha = info['apkSha256'] as String?;` (add this line next to the existing `final apkUrl = info['apkUrl'] as String?;`) and update the call to `await _downloadAndInstall(context, apkUrl, remoteVersion, apkSha);`.

(4) DEPENDENCY: `crypto` is present in pubspec.lock transitively but is NOT a direct dependency in pubspec.yaml. Add `crypto: ^3.0.0` under `dependencies:` in pubspec.yaml so the direct import is declared (run `flutter pub get` after).

Note: `AccumulatorSink` and `Digest` both come from `package:crypto/crypto.dart`; no second import needed.
- **Blast radius:** Touches THREE files: (a) lib/backend/update_checker.dart — signature change to `_downloadAndInstall` (only caller is `_showUpdateDialog` in the same file, so the arity change is contained); (b) pubspec.yaml — add `crypto` direct dep; (c) version.json (repo root, and the release-publishing pipeline that generates it) must start emitting an `apkSha256` field per release or the SHA gate stays in warn-only mode forever. The scheme guard alone has no blast radius beyond this file. The `criticalUpdate` field already present in version.json is unrelated. No other callers of `_downloadAndInstall` exist (grep confirms single call site).
- **Acceptance:** STATIC + UNIT + DEVICE, in that priority:
1. STATIC: `grep -n "scheme.toLowerCase() != 'https'" lib/backend/update_checker.dart` returns the new guard; `grep -n "startChunkedConversion\|expectedSha256" lib/backend/update_checker.dart` returns the hash + gate; `grep -n "^  crypto:" pubspec.yaml` shows the direct dep.
2. UNIT (add test/backend/update_checker_test.dart if none exists — but note `_downloadAndInstall` and the scheme guard are private and coupled to BuildContext/OpenFilex, so extract the two pure predicates to test them): add a top-level or static helper `bool _isTrustedApkScheme(Uri u) => u.scheme.toLowerCase() == 'https';` and assert `_isTrustedApkScheme(Uri.parse('http://x/a.apk')) == false` and `... 'https://github.com/...' == true`; and a helper `bool _shaMatches(String actual, String? expected)` with assertions: expected null → true, matching (case-insensitive) → true, differing → false. Test name: `update_checker apk trust helpers`.
3. DEVICE (the end-to-end install path cannot be proven without hardware): MANUAL/DEVICE on an Android TV box (onn 4K / Shield): publish a version.json whose `apkSha256` deliberately mismatches the release asset, trigger 'Check for updates', and observe the 'file integrity check failed' snackbar and that OpenFilex is NOT invoked; then correct the sha and observe a normal install prompt. This is the only way to confirm OpenFilex handoff still fires on the happy path.

### `lib/channel_tile.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P2×1]

**File notes:** Only ONE finding in this file; no ordering concerns. Two coordinated edits within `_ChannelTileState`, both required for the single fix: (1) add a field to hold the listener callback and register it in initState via `addListener`, (2) call `removeListener` for it in dispose regardless of ownership. No new imports needed. Do NOT change the `if (_ownsFocusNode) _focusNode.dispose();` line — a caller-supplied node must still NOT be disposed by the tile (tv_search_view.dart owns and disposes those); the fix is purely about detaching THIS tile's listener from a possibly-shared node.

#### 152. [P2] channel_tile.dart:~241 — ChannelTile leaks a FocusNode listener per mount on caller-supplied (reused) nodes; stale listeners re-fire pr

- **Anchor:** class _ChannelTileState, in initState — the anonymous listener registered via `_focusNode.addListener(() { if (mounted) setState(() {}); if (_focusNode.hasFocus) { widget.onFocusGained?.call(...); _maybePrewarm(); ... } });` (grep token: `_focusNode.addListener`). The dispose site is `_ChannelTileState.dispose` (grep token: `if (_ownsFocusNode) _focusNode.dispose();`).
- **Current code:**
```dart
    _focusNode.addListener(() {
      if (mounted) setState(() {});
      if (_focusNode.hasFocus) {
        widget.onFocusGained?.call(widget.channel); // fix589 (#5)
        _maybePrewarm();
```
- **Fix:** Hoist the anonymous listener into a named instance field so it can be removed, gate the whole body on `mounted`, and remove it in dispose for BOTH owned and supplied nodes. Concretely:

STEP 1 — Add a field near the other _ChannelTileState fields (e.g. right after `late final bool _ownsFocusNode = widget.focusNode == null;`):
    late final VoidCallback _focusListener = _onFocusChanged;

STEP 2 — Add the handler method to _ChannelTileState (place it just above `void _maybePrewarm()`), lifting the CURRENT listener body verbatim and adding a leading `if (!mounted) return;` so no branch runs after dispose:
    void _onFocusChanged() {
      if (!mounted) return;
      setState(() {});
      if (_focusNode.hasFocus) {
        widget.onFocusGained?.call(widget.channel); // fix589 (#5)
        _maybePrewarm();
        // fix560: ensureVisible in a post-frame callback (see original comment).
        WidgetsBinding.instance.addPostFrameCallback((_) {
          if (!mounted || !_focusNode.hasFocus) return;
          final ctx = _focusNode.context;
          if (ctx == null) return;
          Scrollable.ensureVisible(
            ctx,
            alignment: 0.5,
            duration: const Duration(milliseconds: 200),
            curve: Curves.easeOut,
          );
        });
      }
    }
(Preserve the existing fix560 comment block; it is only paraphrased above for brevity.)

STEP 3 — In initState, replace the anonymous registration `_focusNode.addListener(() { ...entire body... });` (the whole block that currently starts at the snippet through its closing `});`) with:
    _focusNode.addListener(_focusListener);

STEP 4 — In dispose, add the removeListener BEFORE the existing dispose line, keeping that line unchanged:
    _focusNode.removeListener(_focusListener);
    if (_ownsFocusNode) _focusNode.dispose();

Rationale for decisions: (a) `mounted` guard moved to the TOP so the `hasFocus` branch — which currently fires `_maybePrewarm()` and `onFocusGained` even on a disposed State bound to a still-live shared node — no longer runs; the original only guarded `setState`. (b) removeListener runs for owned AND supplied nodes (unconditional) — the leak only manifests on supplied/reused nodes, but removing on an owned node right before disposing it is harmless and keeps the code simple.
- **Blast radius:** Callers passing `focusNode:` to ChannelTile: lib/tv/tv_search_view.dart (reused _nodeCache nodes — the leak source, myNodes[i] at ~line 546), and any other ChannelTile( ... focusNode: ...) sites in lib/home.dart, lib/tv/tv_categories_view.dart, lib/tv/tv_browse_view.dart. This edit is confined to lib/channel_tile.dart; NO second file must change. tv_search_view.dart already disposes its cached nodes in its own dispose (lines 99-102) — leave that as-is. Behavior of owned-node tiles is unchanged (they still create + dispose their own node; now they also removeListener first, which is a no-op-safe cleanup). setState-on-focus, onFocusGained dwell-preview, prewarm, and ensureVisible all keep firing for the CURRENTLY-mounted tile exactly as before.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC (primary): grep lib/channel_tile.dart — confirm exactly one `addListener(_focusListener)` and one `removeListener(_focusListener)`, and that no anonymous `_focusNode.addListener(() {` remains. Confirm dispose contains removeListener ordered before `if (_ownsFocusNode) _focusNode.dispose();`. WIDGET TEST (add test/channel_tile_focus_listener_test.dart, name `ChannelTile removes its focus listener on dispose (supplied node not disposed)`): create a `FocusNode fn` you own, pump a ChannelTile(focusNode: fn, ...) inside a MaterialApp/Scaffold, record `fn` has one listener via `expect(fn.hasListeners, isTrue)`, then pump a different widget to unmount the tile, and assert `expect(fn.hasListeners, isFalse)` and that `fn` was NOT disposed (still callable, e.g. `fn.canRequestFocus` does not throw). This proves the listener is detached and the supplied node survives. The stale-prewarm-HTTP symptom itself is DEVICE-observable only (MANUAL/DEVICE: on an Android TV box, run repeated searches in TvSearchView then focus a result and confirm only the current channel's URL is resolved once — but the hasListeners test is the deterministic gate).
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED from source: initState (channel_tile.dart:241) adds an anonymous closure unconditionally; dispose (channel_tile.dart:293-301) only calls `_focusNode.dispose()` when `_ownsFocusNode`, never removeListener. tv_search_view.dart:421-425 caches FocusNodes per section and 546 passes myNodes[i] — reused by index across searches (comment lines 417-421 say exactly this), so each remount stacks another listener on the same node. The single guard on `mounted` in the current listener only wraps setState; the hasFocus branch (onFocusGained + _maybePrewarm HTTP) can still run for a disposed tile bound to a live shared node.

### `lib/player/cast_controller.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P2×1]

**File notes:** Only ONE finding for this file; no ordering concerns. The entire fix is contained in the static `mimeTypeFor(String url)` method (lines ~117-126) and its downstream consumer `isCastable` (lines ~128-133). No new imports needed. Do NOT touch player.dart — the two call sites (player.dart:365 `isCastable(streamUrl)` and player.dart:1029 `mimeTypeFor(url)`) both consume `mimeTypeFor`/`isCastable` unchanged; fixing the heuristic in-place is transparent to them. The proposed_fix's suggestion to "rewrite Xtream live to the provider's .m3u8 form for casting" is intentionally NOT implemented here: this file has no Source object and no way to know the provider's HLS capability, so that would require plumbing a second file and a provider round-trip — out of scope and higher-risk. The minimal correct change (a) removes the `contains('mpeg')` false-positive that hides the Cast button for any URL with 'mpeg' in host/path, and (b) makes raw extensionless streams (the Xtream live shape) NON-castable rather than a false 'video/mp4', so the button is hidden for streams the Default Media Receiver will reject instead of showing a cast that instantly fails.

#### 153. [P2] cast_controller.dart:~124 — mimeTypeFor substring heuristics misclassify streams: bare contains('mpeg') hides Cast for castable URLs, and  · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** CastController.mimeTypeFor — grep the line `if (u.endsWith('.ts') || u.contains('mpeg')) return 'video/mp2t';` and the trailing `return 'video/mp4';`; also isCastable — grep `return mime != 'video/mp2t';`
- **Current code:**
```dart
    if (u.endsWith('.mkv')) return 'video/x-matroska';
    if (u.endsWith('.ts') || u.contains('mpeg')) return 'video/mp2t';
    return 'video/mp4';
  }
```
- **Fix:** Replace the two lines `if (u.endsWith('.ts') || u.contains('mpeg')) return 'video/mp2t';` and `return 'video/mp4';` with extension-anchored TS detection plus a distinct 'unknown' sentinel for extensionless streams, then make isCastable treat that sentinel as non-castable. Exact replacement for those two lines:

    if (u.endsWith('.ts') ||
        u.endsWith('.mts') ||
        u.endsWith('.m2ts') ||
        u.endsWith('.mpeg') ||
        u.endsWith('.mpg') ||
        u.endsWith('.mp2t')) {
      return 'video/mp2t';
    }
    // No recognized container extension. Bare Xtream live URLs
    // (http://host/user/pass/12345) are raw MPEG-TS that the Default
    // Media Receiver cannot play, so treat unknown as non-castable
    // rather than optimistically claiming video/mp4.
    return 'video/unknown';

Then change isCastable's body from `return mime != 'video/mp2t';` to:

    return mime != 'video/mp2t' && mime != 'video/unknown';

Rationale for the two decisions: (1) drop the anywhere-in-URL `contains('mpeg')` — it false-hides the Cast button for any host/path containing 'mpeg' (e.g. cdn/mpeg4/ paths, tv-mpeg.example.com); TS is now only inferred from a real trailing container extension. (2) Do NOT keep the default 'video/mp4' guess for extensionless URLs — that made isCastable=true for raw Xtream TS, so the button appeared and the cast failed on the receiver; returning 'video/unknown' makes isCastable=false so the button is hidden. .mp4/.m4v/.mkv/.m3u8/.mpd cases above are unchanged and stay castable (mkv castability is a pre-existing choice, left as-is).
- **Blast radius:** Two consumers, both in lib/player.dart and both transparent to this change: player.dart:365 `avail && CastController.isCastable(streamUrl)` gates showing the Cast button — extensionless/raw-TS streams now correctly hide it; player.dart:1029 `contentType: CastController.mimeTypeFor(url)` — because the button is hidden for 'video/unknown', startCast is never reached with that sentinel, so no bogus contentType is sent to the receiver. No other file references mimeTypeFor/isCastable (grep confirms only cast_controller.dart defines them and player.dart consumes them). Behavior tradeoff to flag to reviewer: extensionless HLS/MP4 streams that lack a query/extension marker will now be classified non-castable (button hidden) — acceptable since the receiver could not reliably play them without the correct contentType anyway; this is a deliberate fail-closed choice, not a regression of a working path.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC + unit test (pure Dart, no DB, no device). Add test/cast_mime_type_test.dart with group 'CastController.mimeTypeFor':
  - test('mpeg in path does not force mp2t'): expect(CastController.mimeTypeFor('http://cdn.example.com/mpeg4/12345'), isNot('video/mp2t')); and expect(CastController.isCastable('http://cdn.example.com/mpeg4/12345'), isTrue) IF it has a castable extension — for the extensionless case assert non-castable instead (next bullet).
  - test('bare Xtream live is not castable'): expect(CastController.isCastable('http://host.example.com/user/pass/12345'), isFalse); and expect(CastController.mimeTypeFor('http://host.example.com/user/pass/12345'), equals('video/unknown')).
  - test('true .ts is mp2t and not castable'): expect(CastController.mimeTypeFor('http://h/x/stream.ts'), equals('video/mp2t')); expect(CastController.isCastable('http://h/x/stream.ts'), isFalse).
  - test('.m3u8 stays HLS and castable'): expect(CastController.mimeTypeFor('http://h/live/abc.m3u8?token=1'), equals('application/x-mpegURL')); expect(CastController.isCastable('http://h/live/abc.m3u8?token=1'), isTrue).
  - test('.mp4 stays castable'): expect(CastController.isCastable('http://h/movie/x.mp4'), isTrue).
Done when: `flutter test test/cast_mime_type_test.dart` passes all assertions.
- **Notes:** verify_first=true because case (2) — 'extensionless Xtream live is raw MPEG-TS that the Default Media Receiver cannot play' — is a runtime/receiver claim not provable from this source; before shipping the fail-closed behavior the implementer should confirm on a real Chromecast + Default Media Receiver that a bare Xtream live URL sent as video/mp4 actually fails to play (MANUAL/DEVICE: physical Chromecast, observe cast starts then errors/blank). The URL-classification fix (removing contains('mpeg')) is unconditionally correct and can land regardless. If device testing shows the Default Media Receiver CAN play some extensionless streams, reconsider whether 'video/unknown' should stay castable-as-mp4; the unit tests above still document the intended contract either way.

### `lib/widgets/now_next_strip.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P2×1]

#### 156. [P2] now_next_strip.dart:~30 — NowNextStrip loads once in initState with no didUpdateWidget, no time-based refresh, and no error handling — s

- **Anchor:** class _NowNextStripState — its initState()/_load() pair; grep token `Sql.getNowNext(widget.epgChannelId` and the field decl `(Program?, Program?)? _data;`
- **Current code:**
```dart
class _NowNextStripState extends State<NowNextStrip> {
  (Program?, Program?)? _data;

  @override
  void initState() {
    super.initState();
    _load();
  }

  Future<void> _load() async {
    final data = await Sql.getNowNext(widget.epgChannelId, widget.sourceId);
    if (mounted) setState(() => _data = data);
  }
```
- **Fix:** Replace the snippet with a version that (a) re-loads on widget update, (b) auto-refreshes when the current programme ends, and (c) survives a getNowNext throw. Concretely:

1. Add `import 'dart:async';` at the top of the file (below the existing `package:flutter/material.dart` import). This is the only new import; Program/Sql/SettingsService are already imported.

2. Replace the snippet with:

```
class _NowNextStripState extends State<NowNextStrip> {
  (Program?, Program?)? _data;
  Timer? _rollover;

  @override
  void initState() {
    super.initState();
    _load();
  }

  @override
  void didUpdateWidget(covariant NowNextStrip oldWidget) {
    super.didUpdateWidget(oldWidget);
    if (oldWidget.epgChannelId != widget.epgChannelId ||
        oldWidget.sourceId != widget.sourceId) {
      _rollover?.cancel();
      _data = null; // clear stale channel data while the new load is in flight
      _load();
    }
  }

  @override
  void dispose() {
    _rollover?.cancel();
    super.dispose();
  }

  Future<void> _load() async {
    (Program?, Program?)? data;
    try {
      data = await Sql.getNowNext(widget.epgChannelId, widget.sourceId);
    } catch (_) {
      // Fail soft: leave whatever was on screen; retry on the next
      // didUpdateWidget or scheduled rollover rather than crashing the cell.
      return;
    }
    if (!mounted) return;
    setState(() => _data = data);
    _scheduleRollover(data);
  }

  void _scheduleRollover((Program?, Program?)? data) {
    _rollover?.cancel();
    final now = data?.$1;
    if (now == null) return;
    // Re-query shortly after the current programme's stop so "Now" advances.
    var delay = now.stopTime.difference(DateTime.now()) +
        const Duration(seconds: 2);
    if (delay < const Duration(seconds: 1)) delay = const Duration(seconds: 30);
    // Cap far-future stops (or clock skew) so a bad EPG stop_utc can't overflow
    // the Timer or leave it never firing.
    const maxDelay = Duration(hours: 3);
    if (delay > maxDelay) delay = maxDelay;
    _rollover = Timer(delay, () {
      if (mounted) _load();
    });
  }
}
```

Rationale for the decisions the original proposal left open: (i) schedule the refresh off the CURRENT programme's `stopTime` (Program exposes `stopTime` getter) plus a 2s guard so we re-query just after rollover; (ii) if the computed delay is non-positive (stop already passed / stale data) fall back to a 30s poll instead of a busy loop; (iii) cap at 3h so a corrupt far-future `stop_utc` cannot create a Timer that never fires or overflows; (iv) `_load` catches and swallows the getNowNext error (fail-soft, keep prior content) rather than rethrowing into an uncaught async gap.
- **Blast radius:** Only this widget's State. Both call sites keep working unchanged: lib/channel_tile.dart (~line 782, has onTap:_openSchedule) and lib/multi_view_cell.dart (~line 1111, no key, no onTap). The multi_view_cell site is the one that benefits — element reuse on channel swap now triggers didUpdateWidget->_load. No second file must change; leaving multi_view_cell keyless is fine once didUpdateWidget exists (adding a ValueKey there would be an equally-valid alternative but is NOT required and is out of scope for this file). Timer cancellation in dispose prevents a setState-after-dispose leak in the many-cell multi-view grid.
- **Acceptance:** TEST (widget test, add to test/widgets/now_next_strip_test.dart): `test('NowNextStrip reloads when epgChannelId changes')` — pump a NowNextStrip inside a StatefulBuilder that can rebuild it with a different epgChannelId over a fake Sql.getNowNext returning distinct titles per channel; after swapping the id and pumping, assert `find.textContaining('Channel-B-Now')` and `findsNothing` for the old title. If Sql.getNowNext is not trivially fakeable (static, hits real DB), instead do STATIC: assert the file contains a `didUpdateWidget` overriding on epgChannelId/sourceId, a `Timer? _rollover` cancelled in `dispose`, and a `try/catch` around `Sql.getNowNext`. Rollover timing itself is MANUAL/DEVICE: on an Android TV box in multi-view, watch a cell's strip advance from the ending programme to the next within a few seconds of the real stop time, and confirm swapping that cell to another EPG channel updates the strip immediately.
