```dart
          );
```
- **Fix:** Add the missing cancellation wiring to the retry call so Cancel works during the FTS-recovery pass, matching the first attempt. Minimal change: insert `shouldCancel: () => cancelRequested,` as the last named argument of the retry's Utils.refreshAllSources call, immediately after the onSourceFailed callback's closing `},`. The snippet becomes:

                onSourceFailed: (Source source, Object err) {
                  setSt(() => failedSources.add(source.name));
                },
                shouldCancel: () => cancelRequested,
              );
            },
          );

This is the smallest correct fix and requires no new import or helper. (Optional, larger alternative the implementer MAY choose instead: hoist the entire refreshAllSources invocation — all five callbacks plus shouldCancel — into a single local closure `Future<void> Function((void Function(String)) update) runRefresh` declared once above the try, and call it from both the first attempt and the retry so they cannot drift again. If taken, the first-attempt call at the `shouldCancel: () => cancelRequested,` on the original line ~221 must be replaced by the same closure. The one-line insertion is preferred for minimal blast radius.)
- **Blast radius:** Only affects the FTS-recovery retry path (SQLite code 267 → Sql.rebuildFtsTableFromScratch → retry). Utils.refreshAllSources already accepts and honors shouldCancel (proven by the first call at the `shouldCancel: () => cancelRequested,` line ~221), so no signature/second-file change is needed. Confirm Utils.refreshAllSources's shouldCancel parameter is optional/named (it is used as named in the first call) so the retry compiles. The done-state branch that reports 'Cancelled' (grep `title = 'Cancelled';`, ~line 297) is unchanged and becomes truthful once the retry actually breaks on cancel; no edit needed there.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC (primary): grep the file for `shouldCancel: () => cancelRequested,` and assert it appears TWICE (once in the first refreshAllSources call, once in the retry inside the isMalformedDbError branch); before the fix it appears once. Add a widget test named `sources_refresh_dialog cancel during FTS recovery flags cancellation` that: (1) stubs Utils.refreshAllSources to throw a malformed-DB error (code 267) on first call, (2) stubs Sql.rebuildFtsTableFromScratch to succeed, (3) on the retry call captures the passed `shouldCancel` callback and asserts it is non-null, then taps Cancel and asserts `shouldCancel()` returns true. Full end-to-end cancel-mid-retry behavior on the ~1M-row catalog can only be observed on-device (MANUAL/DEVICE: onn 4K Plus, trigger a code-267 refresh, tap Cancel during the retry, confirm the loop stops between sources rather than running all sources to completion).

#### 161. [P3] settings_service.dart:~231 — Non-defensive int.parse and unchecked ViewType.values[...] indexing in _readFromDb can brick startup on one co · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** static Future<Settings> _readFromDb(); grep the unique token `settings.defaultView = ViewType.values[int.parse(view)];` for the anchor site, and the block of `int.parse(...)` assignments that immediately follow it (the `if (refresh != null) settings.refreshOnStart = int.parse(refresh) == 1;` run through `settings.maxReconnectAttempts = int.parse(maxReconnect);`)
- **Current code:**
```dart
    if (view != null) {
      settings.defaultView = ViewType.values[int.parse(view)];
    }
    if (refresh != null) settings.refreshOnStart = int.parse(refresh) == 1;
```
- **Fix:** Wrap the entire body of _readFromDb's field-assignment section in a single try/catch that degrades gracefully instead of rethrowing, AND harden the one hard-crash site (the ViewType index). Chosen approach (smallest correct change that removes the boot-brick without a large per-field rewrite):

1) Fix the highest-risk crash site (RangeError on forward-versioned index) by matching the elementAtOrNull-with-default pattern already used at line ~170 and ~413. Change:
`      settings.defaultView = ViewType.values[int.parse(view)];`
to:
`      settings.defaultView =
          ViewType.values.elementAtOrNull(int.tryParse(view) ?? 0) ??
              ViewType.all;`
(ViewType.all is the constructor default and viewTypeToString's own fallback; the enum is `all, categories, favorites, history, settings`.)

2) Make one bad legacy value degrade to its default instead of aborting the whole load: wrap the parse section. Immediately after `var settings = Settings();` (before `var view = settingsMap[defaultView];`) there is no try; the parsing runs to line ~419. Enclose the parsing-and-assignment region in try/catch. Concretely, keep the local `var xxx = settingsMap[...]` reads as-is, then wrap the assignment statements (from `if (view != null) {` through the contentTypeFilter block ending at the `}` on the line with `available.contains(parsed) ? parsed : ContentTypeFilter.all;`) in:
`    try {
      <all existing assignment statements unchanged>
    } catch (e, st) {
      AppLog.error('Settings: partial parse failure in _readFromDb; using defaults for unparsed fields', e, st);
    }`
This guarantees reload()/getSettings() always returns a Settings object and main.dart:53 can render.

NOTE the tension: a single try/catch around the whole block means the FIRST bad field aborts parsing of every LATER field (they keep their constructor defaults). That is acceptable and strictly better than the current all-or-nothing app-boot failure, and is the minimal change. If the implementer prefers per-field isolation (one bad key does not affect others), the alternative is to convert the remaining bare `int.parse(x)` gated assignments to `int.tryParse(x) ?? <constructor-default>` individually — but that is a larger, error-prone edit (each field's correct default must be looked up in settings.dart) and is NOT required to fix the boot-brick. Recommend the try/catch wrapper.

Use AppLog.error (already imported via app_logger.dart as AppLog) — confirm the signature; if AppLog.error does not accept (msg, error, stack) use `AppLog.error('...: $e')`.
- **Blast radius:** Behavior change: currently any FormatException/RangeError propagates out of _readFromDb → reload()/getSettings() rethrows → main.dart:53 (`await SettingsService.reload()` before runApp) fails and the app never renders. After the fix, a corrupt/forward-versioned row degrades to defaults and the app boots. Callers affected: getSettings(), reload() (both in this file), and every consumer of SettingsService.cached. The workmanager isolate also calls settings loading in its own isolate (Dart statics are per-isolate) and benefits identically. No second production file must change. Down-side to weigh: silently defaulting a genuinely-bad persisted value means the user's real setting is lost on that field until re-saved — acceptable vs. an unbootable app. The AppLog.error line makes the degradation visible in the log.
- **Acceptance:** Because _readFromDb reads the live DB via Sql.getSettings() it is not directly unit-testable without a DB. Two acceptance options: (A) STATIC: after the edit, `grep -n 'ViewType.values\[int.parse' lib/backend/settings_service.dart` returns nothing, and the whole assignment region is inside a try/catch (grep for the new `catch (e, st)` / AppLog.error line). (B) PREFERRED test-backed: extract the pure map->Settings parsing into a new static helper `static Settings parseSettingsMap(Map<String,String?> m)` that _readFromDb calls after `await Sql.getSettings()`, then add test/settings_read_from_db_parse_test.dart with test 'malformed defaultView index does not throw and falls back to ViewType.all' asserting `SettingsService.parseSettingsMap({'defaultView':'99'}).defaultView == ViewType.all` and test 'non-numeric legacy int value does not throw' asserting `SettingsService.parseSettingsMap({'liveCacheSecs':'abc'})` returns a Settings with the constructor default (does not throw). If the extraction is done, mirror the existing search_method_low_ram_autoset_test.dart style (it already exercises SettingsService.resolveSearchMethod as a pure helper).
- **Notes:** verify_first=true because the FormatException/RangeError path depends on runtime persisted data the implementer cannot observe from source; confirm the boot-fail premise (int.parse throwing, ViewType.values RangeError on out-of-range index) is real before choosing between the wrapper and the per-field variant. The premise is well-founded: Dart `int.parse('abc')` throws FormatException and `List[]` with an out-of-range index throws RangeError; contrast the safe patterns already in this same file at lines ~170 (elementAtOrNull) and ~412 (int.tryParse ?? 0 + elementAtOrNull ?? default).

```dart
    } else if (step == Steps.form) {
```

#### 164. [P3] setup.dart:~251 — selectFile() calls setState after an awaited file-picker with no mounted guard

- **Anchor:** Method selectFile() — grep for `FilePicker.platform.pickFiles()`. The unguarded setState assigns `_pickedM3uPath = path;` and is followed by `_recomputeFormValid();`.
- **Current code:**
```dart
    final path = (await FilePicker.platform.pickFiles())?.files.single.path;
    if (path == null) return false;
    setState(() {
      _pickedM3uPath = path;
    });
```
- **Fix:** Insert a mounted guard immediately after the null check and before setState. Replace the snippet with:

    final path = (await FilePicker.platform.pickFiles())?.files.single.path;
    if (path == null) return false;
    if (!mounted) return false;
    setState(() {
      _pickedM3uPath = path;
    });

Return `false` (not void) because selectFile has a `Future<bool>` return type. The subsequent `_recomputeFormValid()` already begins with its own `if (!mounted) return;`, so no further guard is needed there, but bailing before setState avoids the disposed-State exception entirely.
- **Blast radius:** selectFile() is called from _buildFilePickerField's InkWell onTap (grep `onTap: () => selectFile()`); that call ignores the return value, so returning false on the torn-down path is harmless. Single file (lib/setup.dart).
- **Acceptance:** STATIC: after the edit, `grep -n 'if (!mounted) return false;' lib/setup.dart` shows the guard sitting between the pickFiles await/null-check and the setState in selectFile(). A runtime test is impractical because tearing down the setup flow while the OS file-picker modal is open is not deterministically reproducible in a widget test; static confirmation of the guard is the accepted gate.

Additionally confirm the remaining match is still preceded by the 'keep CPU awake during long playback' comment. ### `lib/backend/conn_timing.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P3×1]

**File notes:** Only one finding for this file, so no ordering concern — but it comprises TWO edits within ConnTiming.probe. Apply the TLS edit (SecureSocket.secure line, lower in the file) FIRST, then the TCP-connect edit (Socket.connect line, above it), so the earlier edit's line offsets don't shift the anchor of the later one. Both edits are inside the same `try` block and are independent of each other in behavior. No shared helper needed; no new imports (SocketException is already available via `import 'dart:io'`). Do NOT touch the `catch`/`finally` — `finally` already destroys `sock`. Note the log-line side effect: TCP-timeout `aborted=` runtimeType changes from TimeoutException to SocketException; adjust any log-string assertions accordingly.

#### 166. [P3] conn_timing.dart:~41 —  · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** ConnTiming.probe — grep for `Socket.connect(addrs.first, port).timeout(limit)` (the TCP connect) and `SecureSocket.secure(sock, host: host).timeout(limit)` (the TLS upgrade)
- **Current code:**
```dart
      sock = await Socket.connect(addrs.first, port).timeout(limit);
      tcp = sw.elapsedMilliseconds;
      if (isTls) {
        sw.reset();
        sock = await SecureSocket.secure(sock, host: host).timeout(limit);
```
- **Fix:** Replace `Future.timeout` on both socket operations with cleanup-aware timeouts so a late-arriving socket is always destroyed. Two edits, both inside the `try` block:

(1) TCP connect — use dart:io's native `timeout:` argument (it cancels the pending connect and throws SocketException on expiry, leaving no leaked socket):
  Change:
    `sock = await Socket.connect(addrs.first, port).timeout(limit);`
  To:
    `sock = await Socket.connect(addrs.first, port, timeout: limit);`

(2) TLS upgrade — `SecureSocket.secure` has no native timeout param, so keep `.timeout(limit)` but supply an `onTimeout` that destroys any socket delivered after the deadline, and assign into a local first so the outer `sock` (the raw TCP socket) still gets destroyed by `finally` on timeout. Change:
    `        sock = await SecureSocket.secure(sock, host: host).timeout(limit);`
  To (note: capture the raw socket in a non-null local for the onTimeout closure):
    `        final raw = sock!;
        sock = await SecureSocket.secure(raw, host: host).timeout(
          limit,
          onTimeout: () {
            // Late TLS completion is discarded; destroy it so no socket leaks.
            // `raw` is still referenced by the outer `sock`/finally for the
            // pre-upgrade case, but SecureSocket.secure consumes it, so on
            // timeout we cannot know if the secure socket materialized; the
            // finally-block destroy on the raw socket handles the pre-TLS leak,
            // and this throw preserves the existing aborted=TimeoutException log.
            throw const SocketException('CONNPROBE tls handshake timed out');
          },
        );`

Do NOT change the outer `catch`/`finally` — `finally` already calls `sock?.destroy()`, and with edit (1) the native timeout throws SocketException (caught, logged as aborted). No new imports are needed (`SocketException` is in dart:io, already imported).
- **Blast radius:** Single method, single file, single caller pattern (ConnTiming.probe is fire-and-forget, gated behind AppLog.enabled). Behavior change is cosmetic in the log line: on TCP timeout the caught exception type changes from `TimeoutException` to `SocketException`, so the `aborted=${e.runtimeType}` log now reads `aborted=SocketException` instead of `aborted=TimeoutException`. If any test or log-scraper asserts on the exact type string, update it. The TLS branch still throws (SocketException) and is still caught, so its log line stays `aborted=SocketException`. No second file must be touched.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC (primary, deterministic): grep the file to confirm `Socket.connect(addrs.first, port, timeout: limit)` is present and no bare `.timeout(limit)` remains on the `Socket.connect(` call; confirm the `SecureSocket.secure(...).timeout(` call now passes an `onTimeout:` callback. Assertion: `grep -c 'Socket.connect(addrs.first, port, timeout: limit)' lib/backend/conn_timing.dart` == 1 and `grep -c 'Socket.connect(addrs.first, port).timeout' lib/backend/conn_timing.dart` == 0. MANUAL/DEVICE (leak, cannot be proven from source): on an Android TV box with debug logging enabled, probe a host that accepts TCP slowly (>5 s) or a firewalled port; the socket-leak fix cannot be asserted by unit test because it depends on OS-level TCP teardown timing after GC — verify by observing that a zapping session across many dead channels does not accumulate open sockets (e.g. `adb shell` inspect /proc/<pid>/fd count stays bounded) rather than growing per probe.
- **Notes:** verify_first=true because the leak is a runtime/native-behavior claim (Future.timeout not cancelling the underlying connect) that cannot be confirmed from Dart source alone. The fix itself is safe and correct regardless — Socket.connect's `timeout:` parameter is documented to cancel and clean up the pending connect — so the implementer can apply it without device access, but should not claim the leak is 'fixed' without the device observation above. The TLS-branch leak is the harder-to-fully-close case: SecureSocket.secure consumes the raw socket, so an onTimeout that fires cannot destroy a secure socket that may still materialize later; this fix bounds the common TCP case and preserves existing logging. If a fully leak-proof TLS path is required, the implementer would need to wrap secure() so the resulting SecureSocket is destroyed in a `.then` guarded by a completed-flag — flag this as a larger change if requested.

### `lib/backend/epg_discovery/epg_validator.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P3×1]

**File notes:** Single finding, single edit site — no ordering concern within this file. The `archive` package (pubspec ^3.6.1) is also available but `dart:io`'s built-in `gzip` codec is the smaller correct choice and needs no new dependency. CROSS-FILE REQUIREMENT: this fix MUST be landed together with an edit to test/epg_discovery_test.dart — the existing `accepts gzip magic (trusts the loader)` test (lines 39-48) feeds a gzip header with no valid deflate payload and expects true; under the fix it becomes false and will fail the suite. Update that test plus add the two new gzip-rejection tests described in acceptance_check in the same commit. Keep `isXmltvGzip` public (still used as the gzip branch predicate and covered by its own test).

#### 167. [P3] epg_validator.dart:~32 — EpgValidator accepts ANY gzip body as valid XMLTV — discovery can stick a bogus EPG URL permanently

- **Anchor:** EpgValidator.isValidEpgResponse — grep for the early-return line `if (isXmltvGzip(body)) return true;` (the only `return true` before the plain-text `<?xml`/`<tv`/`countProgrammes` checks). Fix depends on adding `import 'dart:io' show gzip;` at the top of the file (currently only `import 'package:http/http.dart' as http;`).
- **Current code:**
```dart
    if (isXmltvGzip(body)) return true;

    // Trim leading whitespace, take 8KB, check for `<?xml` + `<tv`.
    final head = _trimLeadingWhitespace(body, 8192);
```
- **Fix:** Do NOT trust the gzip magic bytes alone. When the body is gzip, inflate its head and run the SAME `<?xml`/`<tv`/`<programme` checks as the plain path.

Step 1 — add import at the very top of the file (after the existing http import):
`import 'dart:io' show gzip;`

Step 2 — replace the snippet's first line `if (isXmltvGzip(body)) return true;` and the block that follows so both the gzip and plain paths converge on one validation routine. Concrete edit:

Replace:
```
    if (isXmltvGzip(body)) return true;

    // Trim leading whitespace, take 8KB, check for `<?xml` + `<tv`.
    final head = _trimLeadingWhitespace(body, 8192);
    if (head.isEmpty) return false;
    final asString = String.fromCharCodes(head);
    if (!asString.startsWith('<?xml')) return false;
    if (!asString.contains('<tv')) return false;

    // Reject empty `<tv/>` — the variant walk must continue.
    if (countProgrammes(asString) == 0) return false;

    return true;
```
with:
```
    // Inflate gzip bodies (tolerating truncation), then apply the same
    // structural checks as the plain path. A gzip magic header alone is
    // NOT proof of a valid XMLTV feed — portals gzip HTML/JSON errors too.
    final List<int> plain = isXmltvGzip(body) ? _inflateHead(body) : body;

    // Trim leading whitespace, take 8KB, check for `<?xml` + `<tv`.
    final head = _trimLeadingWhitespace(plain, 8192);
    if (head.isEmpty) return false;
    final asString = String.fromCharCodes(head);
    if (!asString.startsWith('<?xml')) return false;
    if (!asString.contains('<tv')) return false;

    // Reject empty `<tv/>` — the variant walk must continue.
    if (countProgrammes(asString) == 0) return false;

    return true;
```

Step 3 — add a private helper method inside the class (place it just above `_trimLeadingWhitespace`). It inflates up to `headBytesCap` uncompressed bytes and tolerates the near-certain truncation error at the tail of a partial stream:
```
  /// Inflates a gzip body far enough to validate its head. gzip is a
  /// stream codec, so decoding a truncated body throws once it runs off
  /// the end — we catch that and keep whatever was already produced.
  /// Returns [] when nothing could be inflated (corrupt/non-gzip data).
  static List<int> _inflateHead(List<int> body) {
    try {
      final out = gzip.decoder.convert(body);
      return out.length > headBytesCap ? out.sublist(0, headBytesCap) : out;
    } catch (_) {
      return const <int>[];
    }
  }
```
Note: `gzip.decoder.convert(body)` on a valid full body returns the whole inflated document; the 8KB `_trimLeadingWhitespace` slice below already bounds the string work, and the `sublist` guard bounds memory for pathological multi-MB feeds. `isXmltvGzip` stays as-is (still used as the branch predicate); do not delete it.
- **Blast radius:** Three production callers pass real network bytes and only branch on the bool, so no signature change is needed: variants/xtream_m3u_tvg_url.dart (~line 94), variants/stalker_xmltv_cookie_auth.dart (~line 115), variants/stalker_xmltv_query_auth.dart (~line 39). Behavior change: a gzip body that inflates to non-XMLTV (HTML/JSON error, empty `<tv/>`) now returns false, so the variant walk continues instead of persisting a dead URL — this is the intended effect. RISK / must-touch second file: test/epg_discovery_test.dart line 39-48 test `accepts gzip magic (trusts the loader)` feeds `[0x1F,0x8B,0x08,0x00,0x00,0x00,0x00,0x00]` — a gzip HEADER with NO valid deflate payload; it currently expects `isTrue` but will now return false (inflation yields empty). That test MUST be updated in the same change (see acceptance_check) or the suite goes red. `dart:io` import is Android-only-safe here (this package targets Android TV; epg_discovery has no existing web build path) — acceptable.
- **Acceptance:** Add/adjust unit tests in test/epg_discovery_test.dart:
1. REPLACE the broken `accepts gzip magic (trusts the loader)` test: build a REAL gzip of a valid doc and assert true — `final bytes = gzip.encode(utf8.encode('<?xml version="1.0"?><tv><programme /></tv>'));` (add `import 'dart:io' show gzip;`), response 200 `content-type: application/gzip`, `expect(EpgValidator.isValidEpgResponse(resp, bytes), isTrue);` and rename it to `accepts valid gzip'd XMLTV`.
2. ADD test `rejects gzip'd non-XMLTV (error page)`: `final bytes = gzip.encode(utf8.encode('<html><body>403 Forbidden</body></html>'));` 200 gzip → `expect(..., isFalse);`.
3. ADD test `rejects gzip'd empty <tv/>`: `final bytes = gzip.encode(utf8.encode('<?xml version="1.0"?><tv/>'));` 200 gzip → `expect(..., isFalse);`.
Done when `flutter test test/epg_discovery_test.dart` passes with all three. (The existing `isXmltvGzip detects 0x1F 0x8B magic` test is unaffected and must still pass.)

### `lib/backend/search_perf_test.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P3×1]

#### 168. [P3] search_perf_test.dart:~189 — Cold-cache drop runs on the write connection; probe queries run on the read pool, so 'cold' is never cold · ⚠️ VERIFY FIRST

- **Anchor:** SearchPerfTest._dropSqlitePageCache — grep for the unique token "PRAGMA cache_size = 1;" (the method body is two db.execute PRAGMA calls). Related copy lives in lib/widgets/search_perf_dialog.dart, grep token "Cold = the first pass with the database cache cleared".
- **Current code:**
```dart
  static Future<void> _dropSqlitePageCache() async {
    final db = await DbFactory.db;
    await db.execute('PRAGMA cache_size = 1;');
    await db.execute('PRAGMA cache_size = -2000;');
  }
```
- **Fix:** DECISION: Do NOT try to reset the cache on the read pool via readLock — sqlite_async (0.13.0) exposes only a single-connection readLock/readTransaction and no way to enumerate or reset every read-pool connection, so it cannot be made reliably cold and readLock grabs an arbitrary pooled connection that a later serialized getAll may not reuse. Because Sql.search serves every probe through db.getAll (the read pool) while this PRAGMA hits the single write connection, the drop is a no-op for the measured path. Since the finding is cosmetic (recommendation is warm-median-driven and unaffected) and the mechanism cannot be made honest from Dart, REMOVE the misleading mechanism and the cold pretense rather than keep a no-op. Concretely, in THIS file: (1) Delete the _dropSqlitePageCache method entirely (the 5-line snippet above) and delete its call site in _benchmarkMethod — remove the two lines `// Drop SQLite's own page cache ...` comment block and `await _dropSqlitePageCache();` at the top of _benchmarkMethod (grep token "Drop SQLite's own page cache"). (2) Collapse cold to a plain first-pass measurement: keep `final coldTimes = await runPass();` / `final coldMs = medianOf(coldTimes);` but change the `// ── COLD ──` comment (grep "── COLD ── pass 1") to `// ── COLD ── pass 1 = first search after cache invalidation (OS/read-pool page cache NOT flushable from Dart; loose first-hit indicator).` No behavior change to timings — pass 1 was already the first, previously-uncached-in-intent pass. This keeps coldMs meaningful as "first pass" without claiming a cache flush that never happened.
- **Blast radius:** Two files. (A) lib/backend/search_perf_test.dart: removing _dropSqlitePageCache and its call is internal; no other caller (grep confirms _dropSqlitePageCache is defined and called only here). SearchMethodPerfResult.coldMs field and the AppLog line stay. (B) lib/widgets/search_perf_dialog.dart REQUIRED edit: the explanatory copy at the Text widget (grep "Cold and warm run the SAME searches") currently claims 'Cold = the first pass with the database cache cleared.' — change that clause to 'Cold = the first pass (first search after refresh; the OS keeps data cached, so this is only a loose first-hit indicator).' Do NOT remove the cold column render at grep token "Cold ${r.coldMs.toStringAsFixed(0)} ms" — coldMs still holds a real first-pass number. Also soften the class-level doc comment in search_perf_test.dart (grep "We can drop SQLite's OWN page") to stop asserting the app drops SQLite's own page cache between methods, since that code is being removed.
- **Acceptance:** STATIC: grep -n "_dropSqlitePageCache\|PRAGMA cache_size" lib/backend/search_perf_test.dart returns no matches (method and PRAGMAs gone); grep -n "database cache cleared" lib/widgets/search_perf_dialog.dart returns no matches (copy updated). Behavioral: cannot be proven true-cold on device — a truly cold read cannot be forced from Dart (OS file cache + rotating read-pool connections). Add a unit-free static assertion via `flutter analyze lib/backend/search_perf_test.dart lib/widgets/search_perf_dialog.dart` passing with no new warnings. Optional MANUAL/DEVICE (onn 4K / 2GB TV box): run the search-perf dialog on the real 1M-row catalog and confirm the cold vs warm columns still render and the recommendation (warm-median) is unchanged from before the edit — the fix must not alter which method is recommended.

### `test/export_zip_test.dart`  — 1 finding(s) [P3×1]

**File notes:** Single finding — no ordering concerns. Shared context the implementer needs: the app's real export builder is `_buildExportBundle` in lib/settings_view.dart (grep `Future<List<ExportItem>> _buildExportBundle`). It is a PRIVATE instance method on the settings State class and depends on plugin/device services (`getTemporaryDirectory`, `Sql.checkpointAndTruncateWal`, `SettingsIo.buildBackupPayload`, `Utils.appDir`, `AppLog`), so it CANNOT be called from a pure unit test as-is. The credential gate is the `includeCredentials` bool: when false, no `db.sqlite`/`epg.sqlite` snapshot is added AND `SettingsIo.buildBackupPayload(includeCredentials:false)` strips secrets; when true the DBs are copied but deliberately EXCLUDED from the combined zip (see fix536 comment block around line 1819-1842). Any assertion about "what's in the zip" must match those two contracts. Do NOT delete the existing test outright without a replacement — it still guards that ZipFileEncoder produces a re-readable archive, which is the fix328 OOM mechanism.

```
  test('settings backup with credentials excluded contains no source secrets', () async {
    final payload = await SettingsIo.buildBackupPayload(includeCredentials: false);
    expect(payload, isNot(contains('password')));
    expect(payload, isNot(contains('"username"')));
  });
```
If `buildBackupPayload` cannot run headless (it reads settings/DB), gate this test behind the actual seam it needs or convert it to feed a known fixture; do not fabricate a green pass. No production code changes. If `buildBackupPayload` transitively needs Flutter plugin bindings (path_provider/sqlite), the test must call `TestWidgetsFlutterBinding.ensureInitialized()` and may still fail headless — that is the reason verify_first is set.

- **Notes:** P3 test-quality issue: the existing test genuinely exercises only the third-party `archive` package (ZipFileEncoder/ZipDecoder) on hand-authored files with non-timestamped names ('free4me-settings.json' vs the real 'free4me-settings-\$stamp.json'), so it gives false credit to the export feature. The real builder is `_buildExportBundle` (private State method, lib/settings_view.dart) — NOT unit-invokable as-is, which is why the fix pivots to (a) relabeling the smoke test and (b) asserting the actual credential-exclusion contract via `SettingsIo.buildBackupPayload(includeCredentials:false)` and/or a static grep of the DB-gating branch.
